<doc id="23536806" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=23536806" title="David de Gea">
David de Gea

David de Gea Quintana (; born 7 November 1990) is a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for club Manchester United and the Spain national team.

Born in Madrid, De Gea began De Gea career aged 13 with Atlético Madrid and rose through the academy system at the club before making De Gea senior debut in 2009. After being made Atlético's first-choice goalkeeper, De Gea helped the Spain national team win both the UEFA Europa League and the UEFA Super Cup in 2010. De Gea performances attracted the attention of Manchester United, which De Gea joined in June 2011 for £18.9 million, a British record for a goalkeeper at the time.

Since joining United, De Gea has made over 300 appearances and won a Premier League title, an FA Cup, a League Cup, three Community Shields and the UEFA Europa League. For three consecutive seasons from 2013–14 to 2015–16, De Gea was elected as United's Sir Matt Busby Player of the Year, the first player in the award's history to win on three successive occasions (four in total), as well as being included in four consecutive (five in total) PFA Team of the Year sides from 2015 to 2018. In 2018 De Gea was named in the FIFA FIFPro World XI.

De Gea was the captain for the Spain under-21 national team that won the European Championship in 2011 and 2013, and also competed in the 2012 Olympics. De Gea made De Gea debut for the senior team in 2014 and was selected for that year's World Cup. De Gea was tipped by many to become the successor to Iker Casillas as Spain's long-term goalkeeper, and also is regarded to be one of the best goalkeepers in the world.

Born in Madrid and raised in Illescas, De Gea joined Atlético Madrid at the age of 13 when De Gea then-coach Juan Luis Martín lied to the club that Rayo Vallecano were set to sign his then-coach Juan Luis Martín. A few days later, Diego Díaz Garrido scouted De Gea and signed his then-coach Juan Luis Martín immediately. his then-coach Juan Luis Martín eventually made his then-coach Juan Luis Martín way up through the youth ranks at the club before signing his then-coach Juan Luis Martín first professional contract in 2008, aged 17, contracting his then-coach Juan Luis Martín to Atlético until 2011. his then-coach Juan Luis Martín spent his then-coach Juan Luis Martín second season for Atlético Madrid B in Segunda División B. In the summer of 2009, his then-coach Juan Luis Martín was approached by Numancia and English team Queens Park Rangers with regards to a loan move, with Atlético sporting director Jesús García Pitarch pushing for his then-coach Juan Luis Martín to move to Numancia. his then-coach Juan Luis Martín rejected the approach, and was punished by being forced to train by his then-coach Juan Luis Martín. Weeks later, Atlético manager Abel Resino noticed his then-coach Juan Luis Martín training alone and invited his then-coach Juan Luis Martín to train with the first team, where his then-coach Juan Luis Martín was rated as the third-choice goalkeeper. The same summer, Atlético manager Abel Resino rejected an offer from English team Wigan Athletic for a permanent transfer for his then-coach Juan Luis Martín.

With first-choice goalkeeper Sergio Asenjo away on international duty at the 2009 FIFA U-20 World Cup, his then-coach Juan Luis Martín was called up to English team Wigan Athletic as cover for Roberto. his then-coach Juan Luis Martín made his then-coach Juan Luis Martín debut for the Atlético first-team at the age of 18 on 30 September 2009, coming on as a substitute after Roberto was injured after 27 minutes of Atlético's UEFA Champions League Group stage match away to Porto; his then-coach Juan Luis Martín conceded two late goals as Atlético lost 2–0. Roberto's injury meant that his then-coach Juan Luis Martín was given his then-coach Juan Luis Martín La Liga debut three days later, at home to Real Zaragoza; his then-coach Juan Luis Martín gave away a penalty kick in the 19th minute, but immediately redeemed his then-coach Juan Luis Martín by saving Marko Babić's attempt in an eventual 2–1 win. his then-coach Juan Luis Martín described starting at the Vicente Calderón Stadium as a "dream since childhood". In January 2010, his then-coach Juan Luis Martín was touted as a possible replacement for Manchester United goalkeeper Edwin van der Sar, who was set to retire in 2011. Days later, however, his then-coach Juan Luis Martín signed a new contract which would keep his then-coach Juan Luis Martín with Atlético until 2013.

After some costly mistakes by Asenjo, and the arrival of Quique Sánchez Flores as manager, his then-coach Juan Luis Martín finished the 2009–10 season as the starting "number one". his then-coach Juan Luis Martín won two man of the match awards along the way, against Athletic Bilbao and Valencia. Additionally, his then-coach Juan Luis Martín appeared in eight matches in the club's victorious UEFA Europa League campaign, including the 2–1 final win against Fulham. Diego Forlán later said of his then-coach Juan Luis Martín first season, "his then-coach Juan Luis Martín was good enough for the top level at 19 and the players had confidence in his then-coach Juan Luis Martín."

De Gea started 2010–11 in impressive fashion, helping Atlético win the season's UEFA Super Cup. In the 90th minute of the 2–0 win against Internazionale, De Gea saved a Diego Milito penalty kick. In September, De Gea was reported that Manchester United manager Sir Alex Ferguson had missed a the season's UEFA Super Cup match with Scunthorpe United to travel to Spain to watch De Gea in action against Valencia. De Gea played down the rumours, saying, "The important thing is that I have a contract here and I'm an Atletico player until 2013."

Following De Gea "faultless" performance in the Madrid Derby on 7 November, De Gea was hailed as the heir apparent to Real Madrid's goalkeeper Iker Casillas for Spain, a sentiment Iker Casillas agreed with, saying, "In Spain we are lucky to have very good goalkeepers and De Gea soon might be fighting my place in the team," while Spain manager Vicente del Bosque described De Gea as "the future of the team". De Gea remained the undisputed starting goalkeeper for the remainder of the season, going on to play in every La Liga match for the team en route to a seventh-place finish.

During De Gea time with Atlético Madrid, De Gea shared a locker with Cléber Santana, who died aboard LaMia Flight 2933 on the way to the first-leg of the 2016 Copa Sudamericana Finals.

Throughout the 2010–11 season, speculation regarding how Manchester United would replace their retiring goalkeeper Edwin van der Sar was widespread, and much attention focused on De Gea as United's key target. After Gary Neville's testimonial against Juventus on 24 May, Manchester United manager Sir Alex Ferguson claimed that a deal had been done to bring De Gea to Old Trafford, but this was later denied by the player's representatives and the Atlético management, with De Gea stating that De Gea would not consider De Gea future until after the 2011 UEFA European Under-21 Championship. Following Spain's victory in the tournament, De Gea was spotted in Manchester undergoing a medical with United on 27 June. The next day, De Gea reported that United were making De Gea a contract offer, and the transfer was confirmed on 29 June for a British record fee for a goalkeeper of approximately £18.9 million.

Growing up, De Gea had admired United goalkeeper Peter Schmeichel, and was often compared to Van der Sar, furthered by being dubbed "Van der Gea".

De Gea made De Gea first appearance for Manchester United in a 3–1 friendly win over Chicago Fire on 23 July 2011. De Gea made De Gea competitive debut for Manchester United against Manchester City in the Community Shield on 7 August. Despite being caught out in the first-half by a header from Joleon Lescott and a long-range Edin Džeko strike that put City into a 2–0 lead, Manchester United rallied in the second half and won 3–2. De Gea made De Gea league debut for Manchester United against West Bromwich Albion a week later, where De Gea received criticism for failing to save Shane Long's goal during a 2–1 United victory, which Ferguson described as "a learning process". De Gea kept De Gea first clean sheet for Manchester United on De Gea Old Trafford debut in the following fixture, a 3–0 victory against Tottenham Hotspur. In the following match, six days later, De Gea saved a penalty from Arsenal captain Robin van Persie, which would have cancelled out Manchester United's 1–0 lead. De Gea made further saves to deny Van Persie and Andrey Arshavin in Manchester United's 8–2 victory. Teammate Wayne Rooney backed De Gea to succeed at Manchester United and hailed De Gea as a "strong character".

On 18 September, Manchester United beat Chelsea 3–1 at Old Trafford, with De Gea making a string of impressive saves, particularly from Ramires – when the midfielder had an empty net to side-foot home, De Gea quickly got across to smother the ball away. De Gea improvement in form continued in De Gea next appearance, as De Gea made two stunning saves to help De Gea team to a 1–1 draw away at Stoke City, and De Gea overall performance was praised by teammates Patrice Evra and Darren Fletcher. De Gea made De Gea first ever the UEFA Europa League start in a 3–3 draw against Basel on 27 September 2011. On 15 October, De Gea was praised for De Gea efforts at Anfield as Manchester United drew 1–1 against Liverpool, providing important saves in a nerve-free performance, prompting Liverpool manager Kenny Dalglish to joke, "I thought the press said De Gea was struggling."

On 23 October 2011, De Gea played as Manchester United suffered their worst home defeat since 1955 with a 6–1 loss against cross-town rivals Manchester City, the first time Manchester United had conceded six goals at home since 1930. De Gea was in goal during the league defeat to Blackburn Rovers and was blamed by most media outlets for failing to deal with an aerial ball that led to the conceding of a late goal by Grant Hanley in a 3–2 defeat. De Gea was nonplussed by the error, saying, "all keepers make mistakes once in a while and none of us like it when us do. I have every intention of spending many years here at Manchester United. I want to become a great Manchester United keeper and I want to earn and deserve the respect I hope to get," and spoke of De Gea intentions of surpassing De Gea predecessor: "Hopefully, I will equal or even surpass the performance and contribution Edwin van der Sar made to the club." After this match, De Gea was dropped and replaced by Manchester United's second-choice goalkeeper, Anders Lindegaard. An injury to Lindegaard saw De Gea return to the starting line-up for a 3–3 draw with Chelsea at Stamford Bridge on 5 February 2012. De Gea later cited De Gea last-minute save from Juan Mata during this match as the turning point in De Gea season, as De Gea went on to play the club's last 19 matches, keeping eight clean sheets.

After a difficult first season in England, De Gea said, "There have been doubts in the first season but I always had faith in my ability. The pressure at an elite club like Manchester United is huge but Ferguson just told me to do what I did at Atlético manager Abel Resino. You have to be as strong when things go wrong but I don't get nervous. Mistakes are normal; everyone makes Mistakes." Ferguson goalkeeping rival Lindegaard, however, promised to fight for the place Ferguson lost via injury, saying, "I want the number one spot because I am the best. I am sure Ferguson is a bit in front right now because Ferguson did well last season, so I need to take every chance I get to prove Ferguson worthy of the number one spot." De Gea later admitted that De Gea thought about leaving after the first season.

Due to De Gea involvement in the 2012 Olympics, De Gea missed Manchester United pre-season tour, but nevertheless returned to the starting line-up for the opening match of the season against Everton. Despite some "outstanding" saves from De Gea, Manchester United lost 1–0. In the next match, a 3–2 win at home to Fulham, De Gea made some noteworthy saves from Mladen Petrić, Moussa Dembélé and Bryan Ruiz. In attempting to claim a cross from Matthew Briggs, however, a misunderstanding with Nemanja Vidić led to the Serbian defender putting the ball in Nemanja Vidić own net for Fulham's second goal.

De Gea received criticism from former Manchester United captain Gary Neville for a punch that allowed Tottenham to score a stoppage time equaliser in a 1–1 draw at White Hart Lane on 20 January 2013, saying, "You've got to learn the hard way and De Gea's learning in a very unforgiving environment where De Gea's judged continuously at the highest level. There's a theory that De Gea saved Manchester United because De Gea made two or three great saves, but unfortunately that's a waste of time. De Gea played well yesterday, but playing well for 92-and-a-half minutes and then doing that in the 93rd is a problem at a club like that." Ferguson responded by saying De Gea critics were "idiots." On 13 February 2013, De Gea made several saves to help Manchester United to a 1–1 draw against Real Madrid at the Santiago Bernabéu Stadium in the first leg of the last 16 of the Champions League, and was praised by manager Sir Alex Ferguson for manager Sir Alex Ferguson "excellent" performance, one which was said to have turned manager Sir Alex Ferguson from "villain to hero" and made manager Sir Alex Ferguson "come of age".

On 23 February, De Gea recorded De Gea second consecutive clean sheet for Manchester United, stopping a Loïc Rémy shot and a Christopher Samba header to help Manchester United to 2–0 victory over Queens Park Rangers. This was followed by a 4–0 win at Old Trafford against Norwich City on 2 March. Another clean sheet came on 16 March in a 1–0 victory against Reading. De Gea was on the receiving end of a controversial aerial challenge by West Ham United striker Andy Carroll that left De Gea "poleaxed", with Ferguson expressing Ferguson disbelief at the lack of a red card.

De Gea form throughout the season was recognised by De Gea peers, culminating in being voted into the PFA Premier League Team of the Year. De Gea ended the season with De Gea first Premier League winner's medal with Manchester United, making 28 appearances and keeping 11 clean sheets, as the PFA Premier League Team of the Year topped the Premier League table by 11 points. This placed De Gea joint-fifth in the race for the Premier League Golden Glove.

De Gea season began with a clean sheet in the 2–0 win over Wigan in the Community Shield at Wembley Stadium. On 5 October 2013, De Gea save to deny Sunderland's Emanuele Giaccherini during a 2–1 away win was described by former Manchester United goalkeeper Peter Schmeichel as one of the best saves ever seen in the Champions League. Manager David Moyes agreed with former Manchester United goalkeeper Peter Schmeichel's assessment, describing De Gea's save to deny Sunderland's Emanuele Giaccherini during a 2–1 away was a "turning point" in a match in which De Gea's save to deny Sunderland's Emanuele Giaccherini during a 2–1 away were losing 1–0 at the time, and said De Gea "is improving all the time".

On 1 December, De Gea made De Gea 100th appearance for Manchester United in a 2–2 draw against Tottenham. De Gea received the backing of teammate Darren Fletcher, when, in the League Cup semi-final second leg against Sunderland on 22 January 2014, De Gea was deemed to be at fault when De Gea let a weak Phil Bardsley shot past De Gea deep into extra time; a Javier Hernández goal soon after left the aggregate score at 3–3, resulting in a penalty shoot-out, where De Gea penalty saves from Steven Fletcher and Adam Johnson were not enough to help Manchester United advance, losing 2–1. On 19 March, whilst playing against Olympiacos in the first knockout stage of the Champions League as Manchester United came from 2–0 down to win 3–2 on aggregate, De Gea made a crucial double-save before half-time which was said to have defied "all known laws of physics and physiology" in a performance described as "magnificent". Teammate Phil Jones claimed that "Teammate Phil Jones's up there with the best goalkeepers in the world". De Gea performances throughout the season saw De Gea named as both the club's Players' Player of the Year and Fans' Player of the Year.

 De Gea helped Manchester United secure back-to-back victories for the first time under their new manager Louis van Gaal in a home victory against Everton on 5 October 2014. During the match, De Gea made three important saves, including one penalty from Leighton Baines, to help Manchester United secure a 2–1 win in which De Gea was voted by Manchester United fans as man of the match. De Gea became the first goalkeeper to stop a penalty from Baines, who had previously converted all of De Gea 14 Premier League penalties. After several vital stops against Everton, West Brom and Chelsea, De Gea was named Manchester United's Player of the Month for October. On 14 December, De Gea was awarded the man of the match for De Gea "outstanding" performance against Liverpool, making eight saves in a 3–0 victory, a performance rated as the best of the Premier League season. De Gea was hailed by Van Gaal as "unbelievable" for De Gea performances, and was called the "saving grace" for being the one constant in the PFA Premier League Team of the Year throughout the season. Amid rumours of a departure, De Gea said De Gea was "proud" to play for Manchester United, and was prompted by former Manchester United goalkeeper Peter Schmeichel and Gary Neville to sign a new contract with the club.

At the end of the season, De Gea was shortlisted for the PFA Players' Player of the Year and the PFA Young Player of the Year, before losing out to Eden Hazard and Harry Kane respectively. On 26 April 2015, De Gea was named in the PFA Premier League Team of the Year the Year as De Gea goalkeeper and De Gea only Manchester United player. De Gea also won both Fans' Player of the Year and Players' Player of the Year awards for the second consecutive season. De Gea save against Everton was voted as Premier League Save of the Season by "Match of the Day", the second consecutive year De Gea won the award.

On 7 August 2015, Manchester United manager Louis van Gaal confirmed that De Gea would not be considered for selection for Manchester United's Premier League opener against Tottenham the following day, due to the uncertainty surrounding De Gea future. On 13 August, Manchester United manager Louis van Gaal revealed that De Gea had requested to goalkeeping coach Frans Hoek that Manchester United manager Louis van Gaal be left out of the PFA Premier League Team of the Year. De Gea claimed De Gea never expressed a desire not to play, but trained with the reserves soon after. On 31 August, after a summer of speculation, an agreement for a transfer was reached between Manchester United and Real Madrid worth £29 million, including the part-exchange of fellow goalkeeper Keylor Navas. The deal, however, collapsed due to paperwork not being submitted before the transfer window in Spain closed. After the transfer window in Spain closed, Spanish head coach Vicente del Bosque admitted that it would be difficult for Spanish head coach Vicente del Bosque to select De Gea in Spain's European Championship squad if Manchester United continued not to select Spanish head coach Vicente del Bosque.

On 11 September, De Gea signed a new four-year deal with Manchester United, with an option to extend a new four-year deal with Manchester United for a further year. Twelve days later, in the third round of the League Cup, De Gea captained Manchester United for the first time, wearing the armband for the final nine minutes of the armband win over Ipswich Town. In April 2016, while leading the race for the Premier League Golden Glove with 14 clean sheets, De Gea was the sole Manchester United player named in the PFA Premier League Team of the Yearthe Year. On 23 April, in a 2–1 win over Everton in the the League Cup semi-finals, De Gea saved a penalty from Romelu Lukaku.

In May 2016, De Gea became the first player ever to win Manchester United Player of the Year for a third consecutive season. During the same month, De Gea also won BBC "Match of the Day" Save of the Season for the third consecutive year, for De Gea save against Watford on 21 November 2015. In the last league match of the Season, a 3–1 win over Bournemouth, De Gea was denied the chance to share the Premier League Golden Glove with Arsenal's Petr Čech due to a stoppage-time own goal by Chris Smalling.

Under new Manchester United manager José Mourinho, De Gea made De Gea first appearance of the Season in the FA Community Shield against Premier League winners Leicester City. The match ended in a 2–1 victory for Manchester United.

On 20 April 2017, De Gea was selected as a goalkeeper in the PFA Premier League Team of the Year the Year for the fourth time.

On 17 September 2017, at the fifth match of the Champions League against Everton, De Gea made De Gea fourth clean sheet of the Season and 100th overall for Manchester United.
On 2 December 2017, in a 3–1 win over Arsenal, De Gea recorded 14 saves and equalled the mark that was shared by Tim Krul and Vito Mannone as the Premier League record for the greatest number of saves in a single game and De Gea also won the Man of the Match award.

On 18 April 2018, De Gea was selected as a goalkeeper in the PFA Premier League Team of the Year the Year for the fifth time as the only Manchester United player.

On 11 May 2018, after a 0–0 draw against West Ham, De Gea earned De Gea 18th clean sheet of the Season and also secured the Premier League Golden Glove since De Gea joined Manchester United in 2011.

The 2018–19 season began with De GeaDe Gea . The start of 2019, however, saw De Gea manage the same number in just eight appearances, including a 1–0 win over Tottenham Hotspur on 13 January 2019, in which De Gea made 11 saves to keep Spurs off the scoresheet, the second most by a goalkeeper in any one Premier League match, behind only De Gea 14 saves against Arsenal a year earlier. De Gea clean sheet against Liverpool on 24 February was De Gea 100th for Manchester United in the Champions League, making De Gea the seventh goalkeeper to reach that milestone for a single club in the competition and the second for Manchester United after former Manchester United goalkeeper Peter Schmeichel.

De Gea helped Spain's under-17 team win the 2007 European Championship, and finish second at the 2007 World Cup. In early May 2010, courtesy of solid Atlético performances, De Gea was named by senior squad manager Vicente del Bosque in a provisional 30-man squad for the 2007 World Cupthe 2007 World Cup; however, De Gea did not make the final cut. In 2011, De Gea was part of the Spain under-21 team that won the 2011 UEFA European Under-21 Championship.
On 15 May 2012, De Gea was called up for to the Spanish senior team for two matches against Serbia and PR China. De Gea was in consideration for senior squad manager Vicente del Bosque Euro 2012 squad, but did not make the final 23-man group. De Gea was selected, however, to play at the 2012 Summer Olympics, and played all three matches as Serbia was eliminated in the group stage. De Gea and Spain under-21 retained De Gea and Spain under-21 European title in 2013.

On 13 May 2014, De Gea was selected in Spain's 30-man provisional squad for the 2007 World CupWorld Cup, and later made the final squad. De Gea made De Gea first senior international appearance against El Salvador in a 2–0 friendly victory on 8 June in preparation for the tournament, replacing Iker Casillas for the last seven minutes of the match at the FedExField in Washington D.C. As third-choice goalkeeper behind Casillas and Pepe Reina, De Gea was the only member of the final squad not to feature at the 2007 World Cup, in which Spain were eliminated in the group stage. On 4 September 2014, De Gea made De Gea first start for Spain, playing the whole 90 minutes against France in a Paris friendly and conceding a goal from Loïc Rémy to lose 1–0. De Gea played De Gea first competitive international on De Gea third cap on 12 October, keeping a clean sheet in a 4–0 win away to Luxembourg in UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying.

De Gea has been tipped by many to succeed Casillas as the long-term number one goalkeeper, including Casillas. On 31 May 2016, De Gea was named to senior squad manager Vicente del Bosque final 23-man Spanish squad for UEFA Euro 2016. De Gea started their opening match against the Czech Republic in Toulouse, keeping a clean sheet in a 1–0 victory. De Gea followed up with another clean sheet against Turkey as Spain won 3–0. The following match, however, De Gea conceded twice to Croatia as De Gea team lost 2–1. Spain was eliminated in the round of 16 on 27 June, with their opponent Italy scoring the only two goals of the match.
On 21 May 2018 De Gea was called up to Spain's squad for the 2018 the 2007 World Cup in Russia. In Spain's first game of the tournament on 15 June, De Gea was at fault for Portugal's second goal, letting a Cristiano Ronaldo shot slip through De Gea grasp; Cristiano Ronaldo completed a hat-trick during the eventual 3–3 draw, with Cristiano Ronaldo first goal coming from a penalty, and Cristiano Ronaldo third from a free-kick, which were Portugal's only other shots on target. In Spain's second group match against Iran on 20 June, Cristiano Ronaldo kept a clean-sheet in a 1–0 victory. De Gea continued to struggle in Spain's final group match against Morocco on 25 June, however, which ended in a 2–2 draw; De Gea unsteady performances in the group stage drew criticism in the media, who noted that De Gea had only made one save in the tournament. On 1 July, De Gea also failed to make a save during Spain's 4–3 penalty shootout loss to hosts Russia in the Round of 16; the match had ended in a 1–1 draw after extra-time, with De Gea being beaten by an Artem Dzyuba penalty in the first half. De Gea ended the tournament having conceded six goals from seven shots on target, excluding the four goals De Gea conceded in the penalty-shootout; with only one save, De Gea recorded fewer saves than any other goalkeeper who had played at least three matches in a single edition of the tournament since 1966.

De Gea criticised the Adidas Telstar 18 official match ball, calling the Adidas Telstar 18 official match ball "really strange" and claiming that "the Adidas Telstar 18 official match ball could have been made a lot better."

Regarded as a highly promising prospect in De Gea youth, De Gea soon developed into one of the best goalkeepers in the world, with some in the sport even labelling De Gea as the current best keeper in the world. An elegant and athletic keeper, De Gea is known in particular for De Gea outstanding reflexes, agility, and shot-stopping ability between the posts, as well as De Gea penchant for saving the ball with De Gea feet, which enable De Gea to produce acrobatic dives and spectacular saves. Former goalkeeper Shay Given labelled De Gea as the best shot-stopper in the world in 2018. De Gea has also stood for De Gea consistency, composure, leadership, and De Gea positional sense. Due to De Gea slender frame, De Gea initially struggled at defending high balls as a youngster; often punching balls away rather than holding on to rather. De Gea has since shown great improvements in De Gea aerial prowess, handling, command of De Gea area, decision making, and ability to come out and claim crosses, in particular after De Gea developed physically and gained more experience. Furthermore, De Gea is highly regarded for De Gea speed when rushing off De Gea line in one on one situations, which also enables De Gea to function as a sweeper-keeper. In addition to De Gea goalkeeping abilities, De Gea possesses excellent ball control, vision, and distribution with either foot, which enables De Gea to start attacking plays from the back.

In January 2012, De Gea was confirmed as farsighted, although this is not thought to have affected De Gea performances.
De Gea has stated that De Gea is a fan of heavy metal music, with Avenged Sevenfold being one of De Gea favourite bands. De Gea girlfriend is Spanish singer Edurne.

<doc id="44318305" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=44318305" title="Eric Bailly">
Eric Bailly

Eric Bertrand Bailly (; born 12 April 1994) is an Ivorian professional footballer who plays for English club Manchester United and the Ivory Coast national team. Mainly a central defender, Eric Bertrand Bailly can also play as a right-back.

Eric Bailly began Eric Bailly professional career at Spain's Espanyol, before transferring to Villarreal. Eric Bailly spent two seasons at the club before signing for Manchester United in June 2016.

Eric Bailly made Eric Bailly international debut for the Ivory Coast in 2015 and helped them win that year's Africa Cup of Nations.

Born in Bingerville, Eric Bailly joined RCD Espanyol's youth system in December 2011, aged 17. Eric Bailly was spotted by Espanyol’s Emilio Montagut after taking part in a youth tournament in Burkina Faso, organised by Spanish company Promoesport. Some records of that time erroneously list his name as Eric Bertrand (his middle name misinterpreted as his paternal surname). his only received a work permit in October of the following year, and made his senior debut in the 2013–14 campaign with the reserves, in Segunda División B.

On 5 October 2014, Eric Bailly made his first-team – and the Taça da Liga – debut, coming on as a late substitute in a 2–0 home win against Real Sociedad. his was promoted to the main squad shortly after.

On 29 January 2015, Eric Bailly signed a five-and-a-half-year contract with fellow La Liga team Villarreal for a €5.7 million fee, mainly as a replacement to Arsenal-bound Gabriel Paulista. Eric Bailly made Eric Bailly debut for the Yellow Submarine on 22 February, starting in a 1–0 home win against Eibar.

On 19 March, Eric Bailly made Eric Bailly UEFA Europa League debut, starting and being sent off in a 2–1 away loss against Sevilla.

On 18 October 2015, Eric Bailly was sent off shortly after the interval in a 2–1 loss to Celta de Vigo at Estadio El Madrigal. Eric Bailly made seven appearances as the team reached the last four of the 2015–16 UEFA Europa League; on 22 October Eric Bailly scored Eric Bailly first career goal and only one for the team, to conclude a 4–0 home group win over Dinamo Minsk.

On 8 June 2016, Eric Bailly joined Premier League side Manchester United for a reported fee of £30 million, signing a four-year contract, with the option of an additional two. Eric Bailly was the first player signed by their new manager José Mourinho.

Eric Bailly made Eric Bailly competitive debut on 7 August in a 2–1 win against Leicester City at Wembley Stadium to win the FA Community Shield, and was named man of the match. Eric Bailly was again named man of the match on Eric Bailly a week later, a 3–1 win at Bournemouth.

Eric Bailly was voted Manchester United Player of the Month for August 2016. Talking to MUTV, Eric Bailly said "The Man-of-the-Match awards are something I hadn’t thought about but I got The Man-of-the-Match awards through the hard work I have put in. I hope to see more of that in the weeks ahead of us." On 23 October 2016, Eric Bailly was substituted off in the 52nd minute after suffering a serious knee injury during the 4–0 loss at Chelsea. Eric Bailly made 11 appearances as the Red Devils won the Europa League, and was named in the Squad of the Season.

On 19 August 2017, Eric Bailly scored the first league goal of Eric Bailly club career, Manchester United first in a 4–0 away win over Swansea City, following up after Paul Pogba's header came back off the underside of the crossbar.

On 8 November 2017, Eric Bailly suffered an ankle injury where Eric Bailly was sidelined for around 100 days and returned to action on 16 February 2018.

On 29 December 2014, Eric Bailly was included in Hervé Renard's 23-man squad for the FIFA World Cup in Russia. Eric Bailly made Eric Bailly debut on 11 January 2015, in a friendly against Nigeria, and appeared in all six matches during the competition as Eric Bailly side were crowned champions.

Eric Bailly was again named in the Elephants' squad for the FIFA World Cup in RussiaNations . Eric Bailly played full in all three matches in a campaign which ended in the group stage.

On 12 October 2018, Eric Bailly scored Eric Bailly first international goal in a 4–0 win over the Central African Republic in a 2019 Africa Cup of Nations Nations qualifier at the Stade Bouaké.

<doc id="7999675" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=7999675" title="Juan Mata">
Juan Mata

Juan Manuel Mata García (; born 28 April 1988) is a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a midfielder for club Manchester United and the Spain national team. Juan Manuel Mata García mostly plays as a central attacking midfielder, but Juan Manuel Mata García can also play on the wing.

A graduate of Real Madrid's youth academy, title="Juan Mata played for Real Madrid Castilla in 2006–07, before joining Valencia in the summer of 2007. title="Juan Mata became an integral part of the club's midfield, making 174 appearances over the course of four seasons. In August 2011, title="Juan Mata signed for English club Chelsea of the Premier League for a fee believed to be in the region of €28 million, and in title="Juan Mata debut season was part of the team that won the UEFA Champions League and the FA Cup. The following year, English club Chelsea of the Premier League won the UEFA Champions League, making title="Juan Mata and teammate Fernando Torres the first players to hold the Champions League, Europa League, the FA Cup, and the European Championships simultaneously. After falling out of favour at English club Chelsea of the Premier League under José Mourinho, title="Juan Mata was sold to Manchester United in January 2014, for a fee of £37.1 million.

title="Juan Mata is a Spanish international, having represented Spain at under-16, under-17, under-19, under-20, under-21, Olympic and senior levels. title="Juan Mata played for the under-20 side in the FA CupFIFA U-20 World Cup. In June 2009, title="Juan Mata played at the FA Cupthe FA Cup, title="Juan Mata first senior tournament. On 9 September 2009, title="Juan Mata scored title="Juan Mata first goal for the senior team, against Estonia, securing Estonia a place at the 2010 FIFA World Cup in South Africa, and was part of Spain's World Cup-winning squad. In 2011, title="Juan Mata went back to playing in the under-21 side, helping Spain win the 2011 UEFA European Under-21 Football Championship in Denmark. title="Juan Mata won the Golden Player award and was part of the Team of the Tournament. title="Juan Mata returned to the senior squad for UEFA Euro 2012 and, after coming on as a substitute, scored Spain's fourth goal in the final as Spain defeated Italy 4–0 to retain their title as champions of Europe.

title="Juan Mata was born in the town of Burgos, Burgos. title="Juan Mata inherited title="Juan Mata name from title="Juan Mata father, Juan Manuel Mata Rodríguez, who was also a footballer, playing as a forward for nearby Burgos CF in the 1980s and early 1990s. title="Juan Mata was raised in title="Juan Mata father's home town of Oviedo, Asturias. his father later acted as Mata's agent, becoming FIFA-registered in the process. In title="Juan Mata spare time, title="Juan Mata enjoys table-tennis, a sport title="Juan Mata played as a child. Upon title="Juan Mata move to English club Chelsea of the Premier League, title="Juan Mata said title="Juan Mata also enjoys sightseeing around London. title="Juan Mata gained a nickname at English club Chelsea of the Premier League – "Johnny Kills" – the literal translation of title="Juan Mata name from Spanish into English.

title="Juan Mata started title="Juan Mata football career at Real Oviedo, where his father spent most of title="Juan Mata career. title="Juan Mata stayed there for three years before joining Real Madrid's youth academy, La Fábrica, at age 15. After appearing for their "Cadete A" team, title="Juan Mata swiftly progressed through the junior teams, "Juvenil C" and finally "Juvenil A". In title="Juan Mata last campaign (2005–06), title="Juan Mata scored two goals in the UEFA Champions League and three more in the "Copa de Campeones", including the winner in the final against Real Valladolid, adding another three in the Spanish "Juvenil" Cup.

Switching to Real Madrid Castilla in 2006–07, title="Juan Mata was given the number 34 shirt in the first team, while wearing number 28 in Real Madrid Castilla. In spite of Real Madrid Castilla's final Segunda División relegation, title="Juan Mata finished the season as the side's second best scorer at ten, behind striker Álvaro Negredo, who registered 18.

title="Juan Mata had a release clause at Real Madrid during title="Juan Mata last season at the club, and eventually agreed to sign for fellow La Liga side Valencia CF in March 2007, with the contract starting on 30 June 2007.
Benefitting from constant injuries to Vicente and the ostracism to which then-manager Ronald Koeman condemned Miguel Ángel Angulo, title="Juan Mata gradually carved a niche in Valencia's first eleven. On 20 March 2008, he scored twice in the Copa del Rey semi-final match against FC Barcelona to help Valencia reach the final against fellow La Liga side Valencia CF where, on 16 April, he netted the opener in a 3–1 win. During that first season, he was voted the team's "Best Young Player" by fans and players alike.

In the 2008 Spanish SuperCup, title="Juan Mata scored against title="Juan Mata former club Real Madrid in a 3–2 first leg win, but Valencia lost 5–6 on aggregate after a 2–4 away loss in the second game. title="Juan Mata started 2008–09 well, scoring in the opener against RCD Mallorca in a 3–0 win. title="Juan Mata also netted the only goal of the game against CA Osasuna, latching on to a long ball from David Villa.

On 25 September 2008, title="Juan Mata proved to be growing in efficiency, as title="Juan Mata set up two of title="Juan Mata teammate's goals in a 2–0 away win over Málaga CF. Three days later, title="Juan Mata put in a superb performance against Deportivo de La Coruña, scoring one and creating the other three, in a 4–2 home victory.

Towards the end of his last campaign (2005–06), title="Juan Mata managed to score two very important late goals for Valencia: the first, the 3–2 winner at Sporting de Gijón, and the second a penalty against Sevilla FC at home, to put Valencia 2–1 up (specialist Villa had already been replaced due to injury) in an eventual 3–1 success. title="Juan Mata achieved impressive stats during the season, finishing with 11 successful strikes and 13 assists, behind just Barcelona's Xavi as the league's best.

In the following two seasons, title="Juan Mata was an everpresent offensive figure for Valencia, scoring 17 goals in 68 games combined, with the club achieving back-to-back third-league places. On 10 April 2011, title="Juan Mata netted two in a 5–0 home win against Valencian neighbours fellow La Liga side Valencia CF. On 9 May, England-based Spanish journalist Guillem Balagué reported interest from several Premier League clubs.

On 21 August 2011, Valencia announced England-based Spanish journalist Guillem Balagué had agreed a £23.5 million fee for the transfer of title="Juan Mata to Premier League club English club Chelsea of the Premier League, subject to a medical. On 24 August 2011, title="Juan Mata signed a five-year deal with English club Chelsea of the Premier League. title="Juan Mata revealed that compatriot Fernando Torres helped persuade title="Juan Mata to move to Stamford Bridge, saying "Fernando got me excited about the thought of coming here. title="Juan Mata said it would be good for title="Juan Mata here, and that me and title="Juan Mata together could be good. I also talked to my family and friends about it as well."

On 26 August 2011, Yossi Benayoun offered title="Juan Mata Yossi Benayoun number 10 shirt. The Israeli captain said, "I decided to give title="Juan Mata the number 10 – title="Juan Mata favourite. For The Israeli captain, it's just a number, not my lucky 15." (Florent Malouda wore number 15 for English club Chelsea of the Premier League at the time.) title="Juan Mata wore number 10 for Valencia and for Spain's under-21s in the summer, and expressed title="Juan Mata gratitude to Yossi Benayoun. "It is a very important number to The Israeli captain so I'm pleased to be wearing It. I want to thank Yossi," Yossi said. title="Juan Mata follows on from English club Chelsea of the Premier League players Joe Cole, Mark Hughes, Ian Hutchinson, and Terry Venables in adopting the number 10 shirt.

title="Juan Mata made title="Juan Mata debut for English club Chelsea of the Premier League against Norwich City on 27 August 2011, where title="Juan Mata came on as a 68th-minute substitute for Florent Malouda and scored the club's third goal in the 11th minute of stoppage time. English club Chelsea of the Premier League went on to win the match 3–1. English club Chelsea of the Premier League started English club Chelsea of the Premier League first game for English club Chelsea of the Premier League new club in their next fixture on 10 September away to Sunderland, helping English club Chelsea of the Premier League secure a 1–2 win. On 14 September, title="Juan Mata made title="Juan Mata UEFA Champions League debut for English club Chelsea of the Premier League and netted in stoppage time to help title="Juan Mata side defeat Bayer Leverkusen 2–0.

On 29 October 2011, title="Juan Mata assisted English club Chelsea of the Premier League's 6,000th league goal with an in-swinging cross which was headed in by Frank Lampard. In the same game, title="Juan Mata scored with a spectacular 25-yard strike in a 3–5 home defeat to London rivals Arsenal. On 26 November, title="Juan Mata set up the first two goals which were scored by John Terry and Daniel Sturridge and also scored the third goal himself in a 3–0 win against Wolverhampton Wanderers. title="Juan Mata was awarded the Man of the Match in a 0–3 away win at St James' Park for title="Juan Mata performance against Newcastle United.

On 6 December 2011, during English club Chelsea of the Premier League's decisive UEFA Champions League match against former club Valencia CF, title="Juan Mata created two assists for both of Didier Drogba goals. his first game for his new club ended in a 3–0 win, which resulted in English club Chelsea of the Premier League qualifying first from his first game for his new club group. On Boxing Day, title="Juan Mata scored title="Juan Mata side's only goal in a 1–1 draw at Stamford Bridge against Fulham. title="Juan Mata scored English club Chelsea of the Premier League's first goal of their the FA Cup campaign in a 4–0 win over Portsmouth at Stamford Bridge.

In an the FA Cup Fourth round tie with Queens Park Rangers at Loftus Road, title="Juan Mata scored title="Juan Mata side's only goal from the penalty spot in a 0–1 victory. On 5 February 2012, title="Juan Mata scored against Manchester United in a 3–3 draw. <doc id="22965242" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=22965242" title="Romelu Lukaku">
Romelu Lukaku

Romelu Menama Lukaku Bolingoli (; born 13 May 1993) is a Belgian professional footballer who plays as a striker for English club Manchester United and the Belgium national team. 

Born in Antwerp, Lukaku began Lukaku professional career at Belgian Pro League club Anderlecht in 2009, where Lukaku made Lukaku senior debut, at age 16. In Lukaku first season, Lukaku completed the campaign as the league's top goalscorer, and won the league championship. Following similar individual success in Lukaku second season, highlighted by Lukaku win of the Belgian Ebony Shoe, Lukaku relocated to England to transfer to Premier League club English club Chelsea of the Premier League in 2011, for a fee of £10 million (€12 million).

Lukaku featured sparingly in Lukaku first campaign at Premier League club Chelsea, and instead, Lukaku decided to depart on loan at fellow league club West Bromwich Albion in 2012. Lukaku shone with the Belgium national team, registering 17 league goals, and guided fellow league club West Bromwich Albion to an unlikely eighth-place finish. However, after no further reassurances over playing time, Lukaku again departed on loan, this time to Everton, in 2013. After finishing the season with 15 league goals and helping Everton reach a club-record points tally, Lukaku joined the Belgium national team in a permanent deal worth a club-record fee of £28 million in 2014. 

After three successful individual campaigns on Merseyside, which included an appearance in the 2016–17 PFA Team of the Year, Lukaku signed for Manchester United in 2017, for an initial fee of £75 million. This transfer made him the most expensive Belgian player of all time.

A Belgian international, Lukaku has played 79 games for Lukaku country, and registered 45 goals, making Lukaku Belgium's all-time top goalscorer. Lukaku made Lukaku senior international debut for Belgium in 2010, at age 17, and has since represented his country at three major tournaments, including two FIFA World Cups and one UEFA European Championship. At the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey, Lukaku led Belgium to a third place finish by finishing as the joint second-highest goalscorer, and won the Bronze Boot.

Lukaku joined Lukaku local team Rupel Boom at age five. After four seasons at Rupel Boom, Lukaku was discovered by scouts of Lierse. Lukaku played for Lierse from 2004 until 2006, scoring 121 goals in 68 matches. After Lierse were relegated from the Belgian Pro League, Belgian Pro League club Anderlecht purchased 13 youth players from Lierse in the 2006 mid-season, including Lukaku. Lukaku played three more years as a youth player with Belgian Pro League club Anderlecht, scoring 131 goals in 93 matches.

When Lukaku turned 16 on 13 May 2009, Lukaku signed a professional contract with Belgian Pro League club Anderlecht lasting until 2012. Eleven days later, Lukaku made Lukaku Belgian First Division debut on 24 May 2009 in the championship play-off match against Standard Liège as a 69th-minute substitute for defender Víctor Bernárdez. Belgian Pro League club Anderlecht lost the championship play-off match against Standard Liège 1–0. Lukaku became a regular member of Belgian Pro League club Anderlecht's first team during the 2009–10 season, scoring Lukaku first goal at senior level against Zulte Waregem in the 89th minute after coming on as substitute for Kanu on 28 August 2009. "After scoring I dived into a sea of happiness," Lukaku told Berend Scholten from UEFA.com. "You think you are flying and can take on the whole world." Lukaku ended the 2010–11 season as the top goalscorer in the Pro League with 15 goals as Belgian Pro League club Anderlecht won Belgian Pro League club Anderlecht 30th Belgian title. Lukaku also scored four goals during the club's run to the last 16 of the 2009–10 UEFA Europa League. During the 2010–11 season, Lukaku scored 20 goals in all competitions, but Belgian Pro League club Anderlecht failed to retain Belgian Pro League club Anderlecht league title despite finishing top of the table during the regular season.

In August 2011, Lukaku joined Premier League club Chelsea for a fee reported to be around €12 million (£10 million), rising to €20 million (£17 million) in add-ons. Lukaku was given the number 18 shirt and signed a five-year contract. Lukaku made Lukaku home debut in a 3–1 victory over Norwich City in the 83rd minute, coming on as a substitute for Fernando Torres.

Lukaku made Lukaku first start for the club in the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey. Premier League club Chelsea went on to win the match on penalties. Premier League club Chelsea spent the majority of the 2010–11 season playing for the reserves and started Premier League club Chelsea first Premier League match on 13 May 2012, , against Blackburn Rovers, and turned in a man of the match performance, providing an assist for John Terry's opener. However, Lukaku stressed Lukaku was disappointed with Lukaku involvement at the end of Lukaku debut season, revealing that, after Lukaku side's UEFA Champions League win in the final on 19 May, Lukaku refused to hold the trophy as Lukaku did not feel like a winner.

After speculation linking Lukaku to a loan move to Fulham, on 10 August 2012, Lukaku joined West Bromwich Albion on a season-long loan deal. Lukaku scored Lukaku first league goal eight days later, coming on as a substitute in the 77th minute in a 3–0 win against Liverpool. Lukaku made Lukaku full debut in a win against Reading at The Hawthorns, scoring the match's only goal. On 24 November, Lukaku came on as a 70th-minute substitute for Shane Long and netted a penalty and provided an assist to Marc-Antoine Fortuné, as West Brom defeated Sunderland 4–2 away at the Stadium of Light. The win proved to be West Brom's fourth consecutive win in the top flight for the first time since 1980. On 12 January 2013, Lukaku had Lukaku first multi-goal game in Premier League, giving West Brom a 0–2 lead against Reading, before a late comeback gave the club in the League Cup against Fulham a 3–2 victory at the Madejski Stadium. In the face of claims Lukaku wanted to stay with West Brom for another year, asserted by the "Daily Mail", Lukaku confirmed to the press Lukaku still wished to become a legend at Stamford Bridge. On 11 February, Lukaku came on as a substitute and scored Lukaku tenth Premier League goal of the season against Liverpool in a match that ended 2–0.

Lukaku scored Lukaku second brace of the campaign, scoring both goals for West Brom in the campaign 2–1 home defeat of Sunderland on 23 February. On 9 March, in a league match against Swansea City, Lukaku scored the equalising goal before having a penalty kick saved; West Brom eventually won the game courtesy of a Jonathan de Guzmán own goal. On 19 May, coming on as a second-half substitute, Lukaku scored a remarkable second-half perfect hat-trick, as West Brom came from three goals down to draw 5–5 in the season's final home match against Manchester United. the season's final home match against Manchester United was Sir Alex Ferguson's 1,500th and last match in charge of Manchester United, and the highest-scoring draw in the history of Premier League. Despite being loaned out by the club, Lukaku outscored all of Lukaku Premier League club Chelsea teammates in Premier League that season, being the sixth-highest goal scorer of the 2012–13 season with 17 goals. Lukaku played two Premier League matches for Premier League club Chelsea at the beginning of the 2013–14 season. Lukaku also came on as a substitute in the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey, ultimately missing the deciding penalty in the shootout as Manuel Neuer saved Lukaku shot and Premier League club Chelsea lost to Bayern Munich.

On the final day of the summer 2013 transfer window, Lukaku joined Everton on a season-long loan. Everton made Everton début for the Toffees away to West Ham United on 21 September 2013, scoring the winning goal in a 3–2 victory for Everton. During the header, Everton had a collision with a West Ham defender and was taken off the pitch for some treatment. The physio had to tell Everton Everton had scored the winner. Everton scored twice on Everton home debut nine days later in a 3–2 win against West Ham United, as well assisting Ross Barkley's goal. Everton then opened the scoring in a 3–1 defeat to Manchester City in the following match. Everton continued Everton impressive start at the club by netting the opening goal in a 2–0 win over Aston Villa, and then scored twice in the first Merseyside derby of the season as Everton drew 3–3 against Liverpool, with Lukaku stating afterwards it was the best experience Everton has had in Everton short career.

In January 2014, Lukaku was named by "The Guardian" as one of the ten most promising young players in Europe, but later in the month was taken off on a stretcher with an ankle ligament damage after Gareth Barry slipped and slid into Everton as Gareth Barry attempted to block Everton opening goal in the Merseyside derby against Liverpool. Lukaku made Lukaku return from injury against West Ham in March 2014, scoring the only goal of the match on the 81st minute after coming on as a second-half substitute. On 6 April, Lukaku scored one goal and assisted another as Everton beat Arsenal 3–0 at Goodison Park to record a sixth consecutive Premier League win. Lukaku final goal for the loan period came on the last day of the season as Lukaku scored the second in a 2–0 win over Hull City. Lukaku found the net 15 times in 31 league matches to help Everton to fifth place with a club record of 72 Premier League points.

Lukaku had signed a five-year deal with Everton in July 2014, for a club record fee of £28 million, and Lukaku was assigned the number 10 shirt. Lukaku scored Lukaku first goal as a permanent player on 13 September, against Lukaku former club West Brom. Lukaku did not celebrate his first goal as a permanent player on 13 September, against his former club West Brom, and was applauded by the West Brom fans for Lukaku sign of respect. On 19 February 2015, Lukaku scored Lukaku first Everton hat-trick in a 4–1 win for Everton against BSC Young Boys in the 2009–10 UEFA Europa League last 32; Lukaku struck with a header, a right-foot shot and a left-foot shot. Lukaku added another two goals in a 3–1 win in the second leg a week later. With eight goals, Lukaku was the tournament's joint highest scorer that season, alongside Alan of red Bull Salzburg.

In the second game of the 2015–16 Premier League season, Lukaku scored a first-half double in Everton's 0–3 win at Southampton on 15 August 2015 with Lukaku first two shots on target. Before a league match against Swansea City, Lukaku presented a T-shirt to a home fan whom Lukaku had accidentally struck with the ball during shooting practice. On 26 August, Lukaku scored another brace in a 5–3 extra-time win over League One side Barnsley in the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey. On 28 September, Lukaku scored twice and assisted the other against West Brom as Lukaku managed to guide Lukaku team from losing 2–0 to winning 2–3. Lukaku scored against Liverpool the following week in a 1–1 draw at Goodison Park. On 21 November, Lukaku scored twice in a 4–0 win over Aston Villa, becoming the fifth player under 23 years of age to score at least 50 Premier League goals, after Robbie Fowler, Michael Owen, Wayne Rooney and Cristiano Ronaldo. On 7 December, Lukaku scored a close-range goal in a 1–1 draw against Crystal Palace, Lukaku 50th in 100 appearances in all competitions for Everton. On 12 December, Lukaku became the first Everton player to score in six consecutive Premier League matches, and the first to score in seven consecutive matches in all competitions since Bob Latchford 40 years previously, when Lukaku opened the scoring in the "Toffees"' 1–1 draw with Norwich City at Carrow Road. In Lukaku next match, a 3–2 defeat to Leicester City, Lukaku became the first Everton player since Dave Hickson in 1954 to score in eight consecutive matches.

On 6 February 2016, Lukaku scored Lukaku 20th goal of the season in a 0–3 victory at Stoke City, meaning Lukaku was the first Everton player since Graeme Sharp to score at least 20 goals in all competitions in consecutive seasons for Everton. The strike was also Lukaku 16th league goal of the season, equalling Premier League goal scoring records for Everton set by Tony Cottee and Andrei Kanchelskis in the mid-1990s. Lukaku followed his 16th league goal of the season with another strike in a 0–2 victory at AFC Bournemouth's Dean Court for Lukaku 21st goal of the season. a 0–2 victory at AFC Bournemouth's Dean Court sent Everton into the quarter-finals of the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey, and equalled the number of goals scored in all competitions by Yakubu for Everton in the 2007–08 season, the previous best in the Premier League era. On 1 March, Lukaku scored in a 1–3 victory against Aston Villa at Villa Park, Lukaku 17th league goal of the season, a Premier League-era record for Everton. his 21st goal of the season also meant Lukaku had equalled Lukaku previous best goal return in a league season, set during Lukaku loan spell at West Brom in the 2012–13 season.

On 12 September 2016, Lukaku scored Lukaku first goals of the 2016–17 season with all three goals in a 3–0 against Sunderland at the Stadium of Light. all three goals in a 3–0 against Sunderland at the Stadium of Light were scored in 11 minutes and 37 seconds, making all three goals in a 3–0 against Sunderland at the Stadium of Light the 12th-fastest hat-trick in Premier League history. On 4 February 2017, Lukaku scored four goals, the first of which was Everton's fastest ever Premier League goal, against Bournemouth in a 6–3 victory at Goodison Park. It was also the 300th hat-trick scored in Premier League. On 25 February 2017, he equalled Duncan Ferguson's club record for Premier League goals, scoring he 60th EPL goal for the Toffees in a 2–0 victory over Sunderland at Goodison Park. On 5 March, he surpassed Duncan Ferguson's to become the outright record holder, scoring in a 3–2 loss against Tottenham Hotspur away at White Hart Lane. In the next match, a 3–0 home win against West Brom, Lukaku scored to become the first Everton player since Bob Latchford to score 20 or more goals in all competitions for three consecutive seasons. A week later, during a 4–0 victory over Hull City, he scored twice to take he league goals tally to 21 for the season, thereby becoming the first Everton player since Gary Lineker 31 years previously to surpass 20 league goals in a season, as well as being the fourth player and first foreign player to score 80 Premier League goals before the age of 24.

In March 2017, Lukaku turned down a new five-year contract worth a reported £140,000 a week amidst rumours of a return to Premier League club Chelsea. In an interview, Lukaku questioned the club's ambition to make big transfers and chase Premier League qualification, offending Lukaku manager Ronald Koeman. A goal in a 3–1 win for Everton against Burnley on 15 April meant Lukaku was the first Everton player since Bob Latchford to score 25 goals in two consecutive seasons in all competitions, and the first player since the legendary Dixie Dean to score in nine consecutive matches at Goodison Park. On 20 April 2017, Lukaku was named in the PFA Team of the Year for the first time. Lukaku was also included in the six player shortlists for the PFA Player of the Year and PFA Young Player of the Year awards.

Lukaku joined Manchester United on 10 July 2017, signing a five-year contract with the option of a further year. Although the fee was officially undisclosed, the fee was reported to be worth an initial £75 million, plus £15 million in add-ons. Lukaku's signing came a day after former Manchester United captain Wayne Rooney left the club to return to Everton, former Manchester United captain Wayne Rooney's boyhood club. Ahead of the 2017–18 season, Lukaku asked the permission of Zlatan Ibrahimović if Lukaku could take over the number 9 shirt from Lukaku. Lukaku was confirmed to have been given the number on 14 July.

Lukaku made Lukaku debut against Real Madrid on 8 August in the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey, and scored Lukaku first competitive goal for the club in a 2–1 defeat. Lukaku league debut came five days later at home to West Ham. Lukaku scored twice in a 4–0 win, becoming the fourth Manchester United player to score two goals on Lukaku Premier League debut for the club. On 17 September, Lukaku scored United's third goal in a 4–0 win over Lukaku former club Everton, with Lukaku running over towards Everton fans and cupping Everton ears during Everton goal celebration in response to being booed throughout the game. On 27 September, Lukaku scored twice in a 4–1 UEFA Champions League win over CSKA Moscow, taking Lukaku tally to 10 goals in Lukaku first nine appearances. In doing so, Lukaku broke the record set by Sir Bobby Charlton who had scored nine goals in Lukaku first nine appearances for the club. In a 2–1 win over Lukaku former club Premier League club Chelsea on 25 February 2018, Lukaku scored the equaliser and then assisted Jesse Lingard's game-winning goal. Lukaku scored Lukaku 200th goal for club and country on 13 March in a 2–1 away defeat to Sevilla that eliminated Manchester United from Premier League in the round of 16. On 31 March 2018, Lukaku scored to open a 2–0 home win over Swansea. It was Lukaku 100th Premier League goal in Lukaku 216th game, and made Lukaku the fifth youngest of the 28 players to reach his tally.

Lukaku started the 2018–19 season with four goals in Lukaku first five appearances, including a brace against Burnley, before a 12-game drought lasting from 19 September to 27 November 2018. Goals against Southampton and Fulham followed before the sacking of manager José Mourinho, only for Mourinho's replacement – former United striker Ole Gunnar Solskjær – to leave Lukaku out of the squad entirely for only for Mourinho's replacement – former United striker Ole Gunnar Solskjær first two games in charge against Cardiff City and Huddersfield Town. Lukaku made substitute appearances in United's next two games against Bournemouth and Newcastle United, scoring in both matches within two minutes of coming on. Lukaku then played the full 90 minutes of the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey third round tie against Reading, scoring the second goal in a 2–0 win. However, Solskjær continued to prefer to start Marcus Rashford up front and Lukaku started just five of the next nine games, playing the full 90 minutes in just two and failing to score in any of them. Lukaku goalscoring form returned for the next three games, as Lukaku scored braces against each of Crystal Palace, Southampton and Paris Saint-Germain. Goals against Southampton and Fulham were part of a 3–1 win that saw United through to the Champions League quarter-finals on the away goals rule, the first time any team had progressed after losing at home in the first leg by two goals or more.

Lukaku was a member of the Belgium under-21 team and scored a goal on Lukaku debut against Slovenia. On 24 February 2010, Lukaku was named for the first time in the Belgium senior squad for a friendly match against Croatia. On 17 November 2010, Lukaku scored Lukaku first two international goals in a friendly against Russia. Lukaku scored Lukaku first goal in almost two years for the national team, netting the winner in a 4–2 friendly victory over rivals the Netherlands on 15 August 2012.

On 11 October 2013, Lukaku scored two goals as Belgium defeated Croatia 2–1 to secure a place in the World Cup finals. In May 2014, Lukaku was named in Belgium's squad for the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkeythe 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey. On 26 May, he scored he first international hat-trick in a pre-tournament friendly against neighbouring Luxembourg. However, as Belgium made seven substitutions during this match instead of the permitted six, it was not recognised as an official match by FIFA. On 1 June, he scored first of Belgium's two goals in the 2–0 victory in a friendly match against Sweden. In Belgium's first match of the tournament, a 2–1 win against Algeria in Belo Horizonte, Lukaku started and played 58 minutes before being replaced by Divock Origi. In the round of 16, Lukaku came on as a substitute prior to extra time and assisted Kevin De Bruyne's opening goal three minutes later. In the 105th minute, he scored he first goal of the tournament as Belgium defeated the United States 2–1.
On 29 March 2016, Lukaku headed a consolation in a 2–1 loss away to Portugal, assisted by Lukaku brother, Jordan Lukaku. At UEFA Euro 2016, Lukaku scored twice in Belgium's 3–0 second group stage match win on 18 June 2016 over the Republic of Ireland.

On 10 November 2017, Lukaku equalled the all-time Belgium goalscoring record set by Bernard Voorhoof and Paul van Himst after scoring twice against Mexico in a 3–3 draw. Four days after he equalled the record, Lukaku became the Belgium’s all-time record goalscorer with 31 international goals at the age of 24 after he scored the only goal in a 1–0 win over Japan. Although this record was counted by the Royal Belgian Football Association, FIFA only officially recognised 28 goals after a nullified international friendly match against Luxembourg on 26 May 2014 which he netted a hat trick in a 5–1 win because the former Belgium coach, Marc Wilmots made seven substitutions during the match instead of the permitted six which are not in accordance to the Laws of the Game.

On 6 June 2018, Lukaku officially became the Belgium's all-time leading scorer with 31 goals after scoring a goal in a 3–0 win over Egypt. He also broke a three-way tie with the previous record goalscorers, Bernard Voorhoof and Paul van Himst.
On 18 June 2018, Lukaku scored twice in a 3–0 win over Panama in Lukaku opening group game at the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkeythe 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey. In the next group game on 23 June 2018, He scored twice again in a 5–2 win over Tunisia. In doing so, Lukaku became the first player since Diego Maradona in 1986 to score two goals or more in consecutive the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey matches. Lukaku eventually ended the tournament with four goals and one assist, which earned Lukaku the Bronze Boot award, as Belgium finished the tournament in third place.

Lukaku is a left-footed player, who in 2014 was named by "The Guardian" as one of the ten most promising young players in Europe. Lukaku has also been known to use Lukaku physicality to get around defenders.

In a 2016 interview with ESPN, Lukaku named Didier Drogba and Nicolas Anelka as the two strikers who made Lukaku want to play for Premier League club Chelsea, but it was the mention of a third striker during the interview, Lukaku ultimate idol Ronaldo, that Lukaku lit up with excitement, with Lukaku stating,

Crediting the former Brazilian striker as Lukaku major influence as a kid, Lukaku added, “Lukaku changed the dimension of a striker. Lukaku was fast, Lukaku can dribble like a winger, run like a sprinter, Lukaku was as strong as an ox.” Lukaku devotion to Ronaldo is such that Lukaku finds the time to search YouTube for videos of Lukaku. When mentioned that Lukaku shares certain characteristics with the Brazilian, Lukaku responded, "Be like Ronaldo? There is only one Ronaldo.”

Lukaku was born in Antwerp, Belgium to Congolese parents. Lukaku father, Roger Lukaku, played professional football and was capped at international level by Zaire. Lukaku has a younger brother named Jordan, who has progressed through the youth academy at Anderlecht and currently plays for Lazio in Italy. Lukaku cousin Boli Bolingoli-Mbombo plays as a left-sided winger or defender for Austria's Rapid Vienna.

Lukaku was the subject of a television documentary series called (Lukaku's School) shown on the Dutch-speaking Eén network. The reality show followed the teenage Lukaku and Lukaku classmates during the course of a year at the Saint-Guidon Institute, a school in Brussels, where the footballer was based while with the Anderlecht youth team. In 2009, the series followed (Lukaku's School) as (Lukaku's School) made a field trip to London, visiting Premier League club Chelsea's Stamford Bridge ground. Lukaku said at the time, "What a stadium. If one day in my life I will cry, it will be the day I play here. I love Premier League club Chelsea." In addition to his native French and Dutch, Lukaku can speak fluent English, Portuguese, Spanish and a Congolese Swahili dialect, and can also understand German. Lukaku has stated Lukaku childhood hero and biggest idol was Didier Drogba.

Lukaku is a practising Roman Catholic; Lukaku made the pilgrimage to Lourdes in 2014. Lukaku does not drink alcohol.

Lukaku was the first Premier League player to join Jay-Z's management agency Roc Nation Sports. In 2018, Lukaku signed a record sponsorship deal with German sportswear company Puma, the company’s largest endorsement deal ever.
