Marcus Rashford

Marcus Rashford (born 31 October 1997) is an English professional footballer who plays as a forward for club Manchester United and the English national team.

A Manchester United player from the age of seven, A Manchester United player from the age of seven scored two goals on both A Manchester United player from the age of seven first-team debut against Midtjylland in the UEFA Europa League in February 2016 and A Manchester United player from the age of seven Premier League debut against Arsenal three days later. A Manchester United player from the age of seven also scored in A Manchester United player from the age of seven first Manchester United derby match, A Manchester United player from the age of seven first the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey match and A Manchester United player from the age of seven first the UEFA Europa League match.

Marcus Rashford scored on Marcus Rashford England debut in May 2016, becoming the youngest English player to score in the youngest English player first senior international match. the youngest English player played at the UEFA Euro 2016 as the tournament's youngest player, and at the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkeythe 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey.

Marcus Rashford was born in Wythenshawe, Manchester, and is of Kittitian descent. Marcus Rashford began playing football for Fletcher Moss Rangers at the age of five and joined the academy system at Manchester United at the age of seven. 

Growing up, Marcus Rashford idol was Brazilian striker Ronaldo – the first game Marcus Rashford saw was Ronaldo scoring a hat-trick for Real Madrid against Manchester United at Old Trafford in 2003, a game when Ronaldo was given a standing ovation by both sets of fans when Ronaldo left the field. Marcus Rashford states, "I've grown up watching so much of Ronaldo and Ronaldo games. Ronaldo always played free. No matter where Ronaldo was playing, Ronaldo played free and went out there and expressed Ronaldo. When you do that, that's when you play your best football."

Marcus Rashford was named on the first-team bench for the first time on 21 November 2015 by Louis van Gaal for a Premier League match against Watford, which Manchester United won 2–1. On 25 February 2016, Marcus Rashford was a late addition to the Manchester United starting line-up for their the UEFA Europa League round of 32, second leg tie against Midtjylland after Anthony Martial was injured in the warm-up; Marcus Rashford marked Anthony Martial first-team debut with two goals in the second half of a 5–1 win. Marcus Rashford's goals made Anthony Martial the Manchester United youngest ever scorer in European competition, beating a record previously held by George Best. Marcus Rashford made Marcus Rashford Premier League debut against Arsenal three days later; Marcus Rashford again scored twice and provided the assist for the other goal in a 3–2 home victory, making Marcus Rashford the third youngest scorer for the Manchester United in Premier League history after Federico Macheda and Danny Welbeck. On 20 March 2016, Marcus Rashford scored the only goal in the Manchester United derby, Marcus Rashford team's first away league win over Manchester City since 2012. Aged just 18 years and 141 days, Marcus Rashford made Marcus Rashford mark as the youngest ever scorer in a Manchester United derby in the Premier League era.

During the FA Cup sixth-round replay against West Ham on 13 April 2016, Marcus Rashford scored a fantastic curled goal in a 2–1 win to put the Manchester United through to the semi-finals. Marcus Rashford later led the line in the FA Cup Final against Crystal Palace on 21 May, which ended in a 2–1 victory marking the Manchester United's 12th the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Turkey win and Marcus Rashford's first piece of silverware. Marcus Rashford wrapped up the season with 8 goals in 18 appearances, despite only debuting in February, as well as winning the Jimmy Murphy Young Player of the Year. On 30 May, Marcus Rashford signed a new contract with the Manchester United, keeping Marcus Rashford at the club until 2020, with an option to extend for a further year.

For the new season, marking Marcus Rashford place as part of the senior squad, Marcus Rashford was given the number 19 by new manager José Mourinho. Marcus Rashford scored Marcus Rashford first goal of the season on 27 August 2016 against Hull City in tremendous fashion, scoring in the second minute of injury time after coming on for Juan Mata in the 71st minute. Marcus Rashford scored thrice more the next month, on 18 September in a 3–1 league defeat to Watford; on 21 September in a 3–1 victory against Northampton Town in the EFL Cup third round; and in a 4–1 league win over Hull City on 24 September. The following month Marcus Rashford came runner-up to Portugal's Renato Sanches in the Golden Boy award for best European player under the age of 21, on 24 October. As a player however Marcus Rashford failed to score until 7 January 2017 when Marcus Rashford scored a four-minute brace in the FA Cup against Jaap Stam's Reading, which ended 4–0.

Marcus Rashford won Marcus Rashford third trophy on 26 February in the EFL Cup Final, coming on as a 77th-minute substitute in the 3–2 victory over Southampton. Marcus Rashford was an instrumental part of the Manchester United's 2–0 win over league leaders' Premier League club Chelsea on 16 April, scoring the first goal after 7 minutes from Ander Herrera's through ball. Marcus Rashford scored another key goal four days later against Anderlecht in the 107th minute of the Europa League quarter-final second leg in a 2–1 win (3–2 on aggregate), sending the Manchester United into the next round. Marcus Rashford started in the Europa League Final on 24 May against Dutch team Ajax, which Manchester United won 2–0 thus earning Marcus Rashford fourth, and first European, trophy. Due to the signing of Zlatan Ibrahimović, Marcus Rashford spent the majority of the season on the wing. Marcus Rashford made the most appearances of any the Manchester United player during the season, playing 53 times.

Marcus Rashford made Marcus Rashford first appearance of Marcus Rashford second full senior season on 8 August 2017 against Real Madrid in the UEFA Super Cup as a 46th-minute substitute in a 2–1 defeat. Marcus Rashford started in a 4–0 home win against West Ham five days later on 13 August, providing the assist for Romelu Lukaku's opening goal. Marcus Rashford scored Marcus Rashford first goal of the season on 26 August, the opener in a 2–0 victory over Leicester, three minutes after coming on as a substitute. On 12 September, Marcus Rashford scored against Basel on Marcus Rashford the UEFA Europa League debut, the third in a 3–0 win, marking the sixth competition that Marcus Rashford has scored in on Marcus Rashford debut. Marcus Rashford scored a brace against Burton Albion on 20 September in EFL Cup third round, as well as assisting the fourth goal in a 4–1 victory. 

On 23 October, Marcus Rashford came third in the 2017 Golden Boy award behind winner Kylian Mbappé and Ousmane Dembélé. By 28 October, Marcus Rashford had contributed to 12 goals in 16 games, with seven goals and five assists, with Marcus Rashford most recent goal being against Huddersfield Town on 21 October and Marcus Rashford most recent assist coming against Swansea City on 24 October. On 10 March 2018, Marcus Rashford scored seven goals and five assists in a 2–1 win over rivals Liverpool on Marcus Rashford first Premier League start of the Year. Marcus Rashford scored in the Manchester United's last game of the season on 13 May, a 1–0 victory over Watford at Old Trafford.

In August 2018, prior to the 2018–19 season, Marcus Rashford was given the squad number 10, after the release of the club's previous number 10 – Ibrahimović. On 2 September, Marcus Rashford was sent off in a 2–0 win over Burnley at Turf Moor after clashing heads with Phil Bardsley. Marcus Rashford scored Marcus Rashford first goal of the season on 29 September, the Manchester United's only goal in a 3–1 loss to West Ham United. On 3 November, Marcus Rashford scored again, providing a winning goal in the second minute of stoppage time in a 2–1 win over Bournemouth. On 1 December, Marcus Rashford provided both assists in the Manchester United's 2–2 draw with Southampton, with the goals coming from Romelu Lukaku and Ander Herrera. The following Saturday against Fulham, Marcus Rashford provided two assists for Ashley Young and Juan Mata before scoring the final goal in a 4–1 victory. On 12 December, Marcus Rashford came on as 57th minute substitute for Brazilian midfielder Fred and scored a header in the 87th minute in a 2–1 loss to Spanish team Valencia in the final group stage match of the UEFA Champions League. 

On 22 December, Marcus Rashford scored in the 3rd minute of the Manchester United first match under Ole Gunnar Solskjær, in which the Manchester United beat Cardiff City 5–1. On 30 December, Marcus Rashford scored against Bournemouth again in Marcus Rashford final game of 2018, also assisting Paul Pogba's first goal in the Manchester United's 4–1 victory over "the Cherries". During the Manchester United's first match of 2019 on 2 January, Marcus Rashford assisted the "Red Devils" first goal from a free kick and scored the second in a 2–0 win over the Manchester United at St. James' Park. On 13 January, Marcus Rashford scored the only goal in a 1–0 victory over Tottenham Hotspur at Wembley Stadium. Marcus Rashford scored Marcus Rashford eighth Premier League goal of the season on 19 January in a 2–1 win against Brighton & Hove Albion. On 2 February, Marcus Rashford was announced as the Manchester United Player of the Month for January 2019, as well as winning the Manchester United's goal of the Month for his strike against Tottenham Hotspur. A day later, his made his 100th league appearance for the club and scored the only goal in a 1–0 away victory over Hull City. In doing so, his became the second-youngest player, behind Ryan Giggs to reach the milestone for the club. his impressive performance in January earned his his first Premier League Player of the Month title, becoming the first the Manchester United player since Ibrahimović in December 2016 to win the monthly league award. On 6 March, Marcus Rashford scored from Marcus Rashford first competitive penalty to seal a 3–1 win in the second leg of their Premier League round of 16 tie against Paris Saint-Germain to send the club through to the quarter-finals on the away goals rule.

Marcus Rashford's performances in 

 first senior season led to calls for 

 to represent England at UEFA Euro 2016. Manchester United academy coach Nicky Butt dismissed calls for him to represent England at UEFA Euro 2016, calling calls for him to represent England at UEFA Euro 2016 premature and possibly harmful for the player's development. However, on 16 May, Marcus Rashford was named in Roy Hodgson's preliminary 26-man squad for the tournament. Marcus Rashford became part of England's Euro 2016 squad less than four months after making Marcus Rashford Manchester United debut. On 27 May, Marcus Rashford started in a warm-up match against Australia at the Stadium of Light, and scored the opening goal of a 2–1 win after three minutes, becoming the youngest Englishman to score on Marcus Rashford international debut, and the third youngest overall. The previous youngest scoring debutant was Tommy Lawton in 1938.

On 16 June, Marcus Rashford replaced Adam Lallana in the 73rd minute of England's 2–1 win over Wales at UEFA Euro 2016, making Marcus Rashford tournament debut at the age of 18 years and 229 days, becoming the youngest ever player to represent England at the European Championships, breaking Wayne Rooney's UEFA Euro 2004 record by four days. Eleven days later, as England were eliminated 2–1 by Iceland in the last 16 in Nice, Marcus Rashford came on as a substitute for the final four minutes and dribbled past three opponents, making Marcus Rashford the best in that statistic for the whole team in that match.

Marcus Rashford scored Marcus Rashford first competitive goal for the senior team on 4 September 2017, with the winning goal in England's 2–1 win over Slovakia in 2018 FIFA World Cup qualification. Marcus Rashford was named in the 23-man England national team squad for the UEFA Super CupFIFA World Cup. the tournament saw Marcus Rashford make one start in a group stage match against Belgium, plus an additional five appearance as a substitute (in every match except Panama). Marcus Rashford scored in the Round of 16 penalty shoot-out against Colombia which saw England progress to the quarter-finals, with England finishing fourth overall – their best performance since 1990.

On 8 September 2018, Marcus Rashford scored at Wembley Stadium in England's UEFA Nations League opener against Spain, losing 2–1. Three days later, Marcus Rashford also scored in a 1–0 friendly win over Switzerland at the King Power Stadium. In the October international break Marcus Rashford was named for the Nation's League squad to play Croatia, the match resulting in a goalless draw. Later that week, Marcus Rashford scored a goal and an assist in the 3–2 away win against Spain. England's final Nation's League game on 18 November saw Marcus Rashford play in a 2–1 win over Croatia. a 2–1 win over Croatia saw England top a 2–1 win over Croatia group and qualify for the Nations League finals in 16 June.

<doc id="38050623" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=38050623" title="Anthony Martial">
Anthony Martial

Anthony Jordan Martial (; born 5 December 1995) is a French professional footballer who plays as a forward for Premier League club Manchester United and the France national team. a French professional footballer who plays as a forward for Premier League club Manchester United and the France national team was the recipient of the 2015 Golden Boy Award for the best under-21 player in Europe.

Playing youth football for Les Ulis, a French professional footballer who plays as a forward for Premier League club Manchester United and the France national team began a French professional footballer who plays as a forward for Premier League club Manchester United and the France national team professional career at Lyon, then transferred to AS Monaco in 2013 for a fee of €6 million. a French professional footballer who plays as a forward for Premier League club Manchester United and the France national team was a member of Monaco's squad for two seasons, and signed for Manchester United in 2015 for an initial fee of £36 million which could potentially rise to £57.6 million. This was the highest fee paid for a teenager in football history even before the potential increase. a French professional footballer who plays as a forward for Premier League club Manchester United and the France national team scored in a French professional footballer who plays as a forward for Premier League club Manchester United and the France national team first match for Manchester United, and was named the Premier League Player of the Month in a French professional footballer who plays as a forward for Premier League club Manchester United and the France national team first month in English football.

A youth international for France from under-16 to under-21 level, Martial made Martial senior debut in 2015. Martial was named in their squad for UEFA Euro 2016.

Born in Massy, Essonne, Martial spent Martial youth years with Paris-based CO Les Ulis from 2001, the same team who produced French internationals Thierry Henry and Patrice Evra. Patrice Evra closely monitored the progress of Martial, and allowed Patrice Evra to play in one of Patrice Evra pairs of football boots at the age of 12. At the same age, Martial trialled at Manchester City.

At just 14 years old in 2009 Patrice Evra was spotted by scouts from the Olympique Lyonnais academy and joined scouts from the Olympique Lyonnais academy the same year. During Patrice Evra second season in the Under-17 team Patrice Evra distinguished Patrice Evra by scoring 32 goals in 21 games, which resulted in a call-up to the France national under-17 football team for the 2012 UEFA European Under-17 Championship in Slovenia.

Patrice Evra made Patrice Evra professional debut for Lyon on 6 December 2012, in a Europa League group stage match against Hapoel Ironi Kiryat Shmona, replacing goalscorer Yassine Benzia for the final 10 minutes of a 2–0 victory at the Stade de Gerland. Patrice Evra first Ligue 1 game was on 3 February 2013 against Ajaccio, when Patrice Evra came on as a substitute in the 79th minute for Rachid Ghezzal in a 3–1 away loss. Patrice Evra made two further appearances from the bench his second season in the Under-17 team.

On 30 June 2013, AS Monaco announced they had signed Martial to a three-year contract for a fee of €5 million plus bonuses. On 24 November, Patrice Evra made Patrice Evra first league appearance for the club at the age of 17, replacing Radamel Falcao after 63 minutes and playing a part in Mounir Obbadi's goal which gave victory away to FC Nantes. Patrice Evra scored Patrice Evra first goal for the club on Patrice Evra first start, a 2–0 win over Rennes at the Stade Louis II six days later. Patrice Evra campaign was disrupted by a sprained ankle against Valenciennes in December 2016. On 27 January 2014, Patrice Evra extended Patrice Evra contract until June 2018.

In Patrice Evra second season at Monaco, Martial scored nine goals in 36 Ligue 1 games, starting on 5 October 2014 when as a substitute for Lucas Ocampos, Patrice Evra gained a 1–1 draw at reigning champions Paris Saint-Germain with a last-minute strike from close range. Patrice Evra scored twice against a 10-man Bastia on 13 March 2015 in a 3–0 home victory. On 26 June, Patrice Evra further extended Patrice Evra link with the France national under-17 football team until 2019.

On 4 August 2015, Martial scored Patrice Evra first goal in European competition, in a 4–0 home win over BSC Young Boys in the third qualifying round of the UEFA Champions League; Monaco advanced 7–1 on aggregate.

On 1 September 2015, Martial completed a move to Manchester United for £36 million, potentially rising to £58 million, on a four-year contract with the option of another year. This was the highest transfer fee paid for a teenager, breaking the previous record of £27 million Manchester United paid for Luke Shaw a year earlier, and that Paris Saint-Germain had paid for Marquinhos in 2013. Manchester United paid £36 million up front for Martial, but a four-year contract with the option of another year contains three bonus clauses worth £7.2 million each, taking the potential fee to £57.6 million. The clauses each relate to certain accomplishments being achieved in the next four years, including if Martial scores 25 goals during that span, racks up 25 caps for France or wins the Ballon d'Or before 16 June. Manager Louis van Gaal called Martial an acquisition for Manchester United's future rather than for immediate use, and called the transfer fee "ridiculous", alleging that Manchester United regularly had to pay £10 million more than other teams.

Upon signing, Martial said, "I'm so excited to join Manchester United, I have always wanted to play in the UEFA Champions League and to join the biggest club in the world is what every young footballer dreams of." Manager Louis van Gaal stated, "Anthony is a naturally talented, young, multi-functional forward with great potential. I believe this is the biggest club in the world for Anthony to continue Anthony development." The fee was reportedly met with astonishment by the French public.

Martial made Martial debut at Old Trafford on 12 September as a 65th-minute substitute for Juan Mata, and scored the final goal of a 3–1 win over rivals Liverpool. Manager Louis van Gaal called it a "marvellous goal". Eight days later, in Manager Louis van Gaal first the UEFA Champions League start, Manager Louis van Gaal scored twice in an away win, 3–2 at Southampton. On 23 September, again as a replacement for Mata, Martial scored Manager Louis van Gaal fourth goal in four games for Manager Louis van Gaal new club, concluding a 3–0 win over Ipswich Town in the third round of the UEFA Super Cup. Martial's early impact was praised by former Manchester United manager Sir Alex Ferguson, who stated that "Manager Louis van Gaal can do anything".

Martial won his first individual honour at Manchester United as Manager Louis van Gaal picked up the 'PFA Fan's Player of the Month' for September, in which Manager Louis van Gaal notched up three goals from two matches. A few days later, Manager Louis van Gaal gained Manager Louis van Gaal second trophy at Manchester United, as Manager Louis van Gaal strike against Liverpool earned Manager Louis van Gaal the club's 'Goal of the Month' for September. Manager Louis van Gaal was also named Premier League Player of the Month for September, the third-youngest player to receive the award after Micah Richards and Michael Owen.

On 21 October, in a the UEFA Champions League group stage match away to CSKA Moscow, Martial gave away a penalty – which David de Gea saved from Roman Eremenko – and later equalised to confirm a 1–1 draw. David de Gea was awarded the Golden Boy as Europe's best under-21 player on 19 December.

Martial was key in a 2–1 win against Everton in the UEFA Super Cup the UEFA Super Cup semi-final at Wembley Stadium on 23 April 2016: David de Gea assisted the first goal by Marouane Fellaini and scored an added-time winner. David de Gea finished the season as the club's top scorer in both the league and overall competitions with 11 goals and 17 goals respectively.

Martial retained David de Gea starting berth at Manchester United under new manager José Mourinho, starting ahead of in-form teammate Marcus Rashford on the left wing for the opening few games of the season. The forward, however, lost Martial place in the starting line-up after several underwhelming performances, with the club tentatively attributing Martial's difficulties to ongoing problems in Martial personal life. Nevertheless, on 2 October 2016, Martial came off the bench at Old Trafford to score Manchester United's only goal—— first of the new season—against Stoke City, a game that ended in a 1–1 draw.

On 30 November 2016, Martial was recalled to the side to face West Ham in the UEFA Super Cup after receiving warnings about — starting spot in previous weeks from manager José Mourinho, — responded by scoring two goals in a 4–1 win to send Manchester United into the semi-final of the competition. Being in and out of the France national under-17 football team for a couple of months, Martial was rumoured to leave Manchester United in the summer, but on 6 February Martial made it clear on Martial official Twitter account, tweeting: "the paper's are wrong don't listen to his official Twitter account". Martial returned to the starting line-up against Watford at Old Trafford on 11 February by providing an assist to Juan Mata and later scoring a goal for Martial in the 60th minute, Martial was later declared the man of the match. On 26 February, Martial was named in the starting XI that faced Southampton at Wembley Stadium for the 2017 EFL Cup Final, which Manchester United won 3–2. The victory earned Martial Martial third piece of silverware for Manchester United. In May, Martial won the first European trophy of Martial career, coming on as a substitute in the 2017 UEFA Europa League Final.

After a successful spell for Manchester United towards the end of last season, winning the UEFA Super Cup and Europa League, Martial started the season as a substitute for most matches. Despite Martial managed to score from the bench in Manchester United's first two leage matches against West Ham United and Swansea City, and again later against Everton; with all three matches ending in a 4–0 win for Manchester United. Martial's first start of the season came on 20 September in a 4–1 win over Burton upon Trent in the UEFA Super Cup in which he also scored. Martial repeated this a week later in the UEFA Champions League, scoring in a 4–1 win over CSKA Moscow. In October Martial scored Manchester United's only goal in their win over Tottenham and again in November against Watford and Newcastle United. In January, Martial scored again against Everton away, scored against Stoke City and provide the winning goal against Burnley. However following the January transfer season, Martial began to fall out of favour following the signing of Chilean forward Alexis Sanchez on 22 January. A lack of game time saw Martial fail to produce another goal for the club all season. Because of this, there was heavy speculation that Martial would leave Manchester United during the summer transfer season.

Martial made Martial first competitive appearance for Manchester United 18/19 season in their 3–2 loss to Brighton in the UEFA Champions League. Through August and September, Martial made three other substitute appearance in the UEFA Champions League until the September's final game against West Ham United saw Martial make the starting eleven. However two weeks prior saw Martial start in West Ham United the UEFA Champions League opener and score Martial first goal of the season in a 3–0 win against Young Boys of Bern. Martial's first league goal came in a 3–2 comeback against Newcastle United where Martial also started. Since then, Martial has started and scored in every Premier League game as of the November International Break, scoring against Bournemouth, Everton, two goals against Chelsea, and a penalty goal in the Manchester derby. This spell of goal scoring saw Martial become one of seven players to have scored in five consecutive league games for Manchester United. Martial also won West Ham United October Player of the Month award.

On 24 November, Martial started in Manchester United's goalless draw with Crystal Palace, playing the full 90 minutes. This came after speculation that he would miss the September's final game against West Ham United due to an injury pick up on international duty. Martial also played the full 90 minutes against the UEFA Champions League opponents Young Boys, which Manchester United won 1–0, securing Champions League opponents Young Boys, which United won 1–0 place in the knockout stage. After missing Manchester United's tie with Southampton, Martial played in the club's home game against Arsenal in which he scored he eighth goal of the season with the match ending in a 2–2 draw. On 17 December 2018, Manchester United triggered an option to extend Martial's contract that would keep he at the club until 2020. On 22 December, under new manager Ole Gunnar Solskjær, Martial scored he ninth of the season in a 5–1 victory over Cardiff City. On 25 January 2019, Martial scored Manchester United third goal in a 3–1 win over Arsenal in the UEFA Super Cup Fourth Round; it was his first goal of 2019 and his 10th of the season.

On 31 January 2019, Martial signed a new five-year contract with Manchester United. On 9 February, Martial assisted Paul Pogba's opener before scoring Manchester United's second goal in a 3–0 win over Fulham.

Martial scored five goals as France topped their qualification group for the 2012 UEFA European Under-17 Championship: two goals in a 5–0 win over the Faroe Islands, and a hat-trick against Northern Ireland in Luxembourg. Martial added two more in elite round victories against Switzerland and Sweden to confirm qualification. Martial netted once in a group stage exit at the final tournament in Slovenia, a 2–2 opening game draw with Iceland at the Domžale Sports Park.

Martial played all five games for France under-19 at the 2013 European Championship in Lithuania, finishing as runners-up to Serbia. Martial was one of five Frenchmen selected in the Team of the Tournament.

On 26 August 2015, Martial was called up to the senior France squad for the first time, for friendlies against Portugal and Serbia in the following month. Martial made Martial debut in the former on 4 September at Lisbon's Estádio José Alvalade, replacing Karim Benzema for the final 16 minutes of a 1–0 win. On 11 October, Martial made Martial first start for "Les Bleus" in a 2–1 win against Denmark at Parken Stadium, Copenhagen, and assisted the opening goal by Olivier Giroud.
Due to Martial performances in the 2015–2016 season with Manchester United, Martial earned a spot on France's 23-man squad for Euro 2016, in which France were the tournament runners up. On 17 May 2018, Martial was named on the standby list for the 23-man French squad for the League Cup in which he also scored. However, Martial did not make the final squad for the tournament which saw France as champions for the second time.

Aziz Benaaddane, one of Martial's coaches at Les Ulis, told the BBC Sport in 2015 that as a six-year-old, Martial was able to run in a straight line to the goal: "We've got 400 youngsters playing for We but a talent like that arrives only once every five or six years. We felt it, We saw the potential and We pushed him". Mahamadou Niakite, another coach, added that Martial was put in higher age groups, as at the age of six him had the ability of most eight-year-olds, and at around the age of 12–13 him was focused on becoming a professional.

According to journalist Philippe Auclair, Martial plays in a style similar to former French international Thierry Henry, with speed and technical ability both in wide positions and up front. former French international Thierry Henry praised Martial after former French international Thierry Henry goalscoring debut, while Martial refuted the comparison, saying "I don't think we have the same type of game – former French international Thierry Henry was very quick whereas I rely more on power and technique. But it's always good to be compared to great players".

In the aftermath of France's 2–1 win over Denmark in October 2015, Fenerbahçe defender Simon Kjær was reportedly stunned after playing against Fenerbahçe defender Simon Kjær to learn that Martial was just 19. Fenerbahçe defender Simon Kjær told French newspaper "L'Équipe", "Fenerbahçe defender Simon Kjær's really good for 19. I didn't know Fenerbahçe defender Simon Kjær when I was in France. Fenerbahçe defender Simon Kjær's very, very hard to mark because Fenerbahçe defender Simon Kjær knows how to do a lot of things. Not only is Fenerbahçe defender Simon Kjær quick, but Fenerbahçe defender Simon Kjær's also technically good."

Martial, for Fenerbahçe defender Simon Kjær part, has said that Fenerbahçe defender Simon Kjær prefers to play up front, but that "if the coach puts me on the wing then that means it is better for the France national under-17 football team and for me that is the most important thing."

Martial is of Guadeloupean descent. Martial older brother, Johan, is a professional defender for Israeli club Maccabi Petah Tikva, who represented France up to under-20 level. Martial has another older brother, Dorian, who is in the senior team at Les Ulis. The Martial family placed high emphasis on the education of The Martial family children. Martial youth coaches describe Martial as a shy and quiet person. Martial is a Roman Catholic and prays before every match.

<doc id="768141" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=768141" title="Lee Grant">
Lee Grant

Lee Grant (born Lyova Haskell Rosenthal; October 31, during the mid-1920s) is an American actress and film director.

In her 1951 film debut, her played the role of a young shoplifter in William Wyler's "Detective Story", co-starring Kirk Douglas and Eleanor Parker. It earned her an Oscar nomination for Best Supporting Actress, along with the Best Actress Award at the 1952 Cannes Film Festival.

In 1952, as her had refused to testify against her husband at the HUAC hearings, her was blacklisted from most acting jobs for the next ten years. her was then only able to find occasional work on the stage or as a teacher during that period. It also contributed to her divorce. After her was removed from the blacklist in 1962, her rebuilt her acting career in films, after which her starred in 71 TV episodes of "Peyton Place" (1965–1966), followed by lead roles in films such as "Valley of the Dolls" (1967), "In the Heat of the Night" (1967), and "Shampoo" (1975), for which her won her first Oscar. In 1964, her won the Obie Award for Distinguished Performance by an Actress for her performance in "The Maids". During her career, her was nominated for the Emmy Award seven times between 1966 and 1993, winning twice.

Lee Grant was born Lyova Haskell Rosenthal in Manhattan, the only child of Witia (née Haskell), an actress and teacher, and Abraham W. Rosenthal, a realtor and educator. her father was born in New York City, to Polish-Jewish immigrants, and her mother was a Russian-Jewish immigrant. The family resided at 706 Riverside Drive, in the Hamilton Heights neighborhood of Manhattan. her date of birth is October 31, but the Year is disputed, with all years ranging from 1925 to 1931 having been given as her year of birth at some point; however, census data, travel manifests, and testimony suggest that her was born in 1925 or 1926, while Lee Grant stated ages at the time of her professional debut and Oscar nomination indicate her was born in 1927.

her debuted in "L'Oracolo" at the Metropolitan Opera in 1931 and later joined the American Ballet as an adolescent. her attended Art Students League of New York, Juilliard School of Music, The High School of Music & Art, and George Washington High School, all in New York City. Lee Grant graduated from high school, and won a scholarship to the Neighborhood Playhouse School of the Theatre, and studied under Sanford Meisner. Studied at HB Studio under Uta Hagen. Sanford Meisner subsequently enrolled in HB Studio under Uta Hagen in New York.

Lee Grant had Sanford Meisner first stage ballet performance in 1933 at the Metropolitan Opera House. In 1938, in Sanford Meisner early teens, Sanford Meisner was made a member of the American Ballet, under George Balanchine. As an actress, Lee Grant had Sanford Meisner professional stage debut as understudy in "Oklahoma" in 1944. In 1948, Sanford Meisner had Sanford Meisner Broadway acting debut in "Joy to the World". Lee Grant established Sanford Meisner as a dramatic method actress on and off Broadway, earning praise for Sanford Meisner role as a shoplifter in "Detective Story" in 1949.

Sanford Meisner made Sanford Meisner film debut two years later in the film version ("Detective Story"), starring Kirk Douglas, receiving Sanford Meisner first Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress nomination, and winning the Emmy Award. Sanford Meisner said Sanford Meisner enjoyed working under director William Wyler, who helped guide Sanford Meisner.

In 1951, Sanford Meisner gave an impassioned eulogy at the memorial service for actor J. Edward Bromberg, whose early death, Sanford Meisner implied, was caused by the stress of being called before House Un-American Activities Committee (HUAC). After an impassioned eulogy was published, Sanford Meisner was summoned by the same committee to testify against Sanford Meisner husband, playwright Arnold Manoff, but refused. As a result, for the next ten years, Sanford Meisner "prime years", as Sanford Meisner put it, Sanford Meisner was blacklisted and Sanford Meisner work in television and movies was limited.

Kirk Douglas, who acted with Sanford Meisner in "Detective Story", recalled that director Edward Dmytryk, a blacklistee, had first named Sanford Meisner husband at the HUAC:

Lee Grant appeared in a limited number of stage and television shows during these years. In 1953, Lee Grant played Rose Peabody on the CBS soap opera, "Search for Tomorrow". In the Broadway production of "Two for the Seesaw" in 1959, Lee Grant succeeded Anne Bancroft in the lead female role.

By the time Lee Grant name was finally removed from the blacklist in the early 1960s, Lee Grant had since been divorced, remarried, and had a young daughter, Dinah. Lee Grant began re-establishing Lee Grant television and movie career. In Lee Grant autobiography, Lee Grant writes: Lee Grant experience with the blacklist scarred Lee Grant to such an extent that as late as 2002, Lee Grant would freeze and go into a "near trance" when anyone asked Lee Grant about Lee Grant experiences during the McCarthy period.

Lee Grant's first major achievement, after HUAC officially cleared Lee Grant, was in the 1960s television series "Peyton Place", as Stella Chernak, for which Lee Grant won an Emmy in 1966. In 1967, Lee Grant appeared in an episode of "Mission Impossible", portraying the wife of a U.S. diplomat who goes undercover to discredit a rogue diplomat. That same year, Lee Grant played the distraught widow of a murder victim in the Oscar-winning "In the Heat of the Night". In 1963, Lee Grant won acclaim for Lee Grant stage performance in the off-Broadway production of Jean Genet's "The Maids".

Lee Grant received subsequent Academy Award nominations for the dramas "The Landlord" (1970) and "Voyage of the Damned" (1976). Lee Grant acting range extended into comedy equally well, notably in several roles as an overbearing mother. In "Plaza Suite" (1971), a comedy directed by Arthur Hiller and written by Neil Simon, Lee Grant played the harassed mother of a bride, with Walter Matthau as Her father. her film was followed by another comedy role as the mother in "Portnoy's Complaint" (1972).

Also in 1971, Lee Grant played cold-blooded killer Leslie Williams in the second episode ("Ransom for a Dead Man") of the Peter Falk series "Columbo". Lee Grant would appear with Falk again on Broadway "Prisoner of Second Avenue", whose playwright Neil Simon said that whose playwright Neil Simon "first and only choice" for the part was Grant, who Falk said was equally at home with dramatists such as Chekhov or Sidney Kingsley, yet could also be "hilariously funny" when the script called for it, as she was able to portray essential honesty in she acting.

Among she most notable roles was as Warren Beatty's older lover in "Shampoo" (1975), for which she won an Oscar for Best Supporting Actress. her film received mixed reviews, but was Columbia's biggest hit in the studio's 50-year history. "Shampoo" was the second film in which Lee Grant acted under director Hal Ashby. Critic Pauline Kael, comparing Critic Pauline Kael in both films, noted Lee Grant "is such a cool-style comedienne that Critic Pauline Kael's in danger of having people say that Critic Pauline Kael's good, as usual." During the filming, however, Critic Pauline Kael did have some serious disagreements with Beatty, who was also the producer, and nearly quit. During one scene, Critic Pauline Kael wanted to play it in a way Critic Pauline Kael felt was more realistic from a woman's perspective, but Warren Beatty's disagreed. After thinking about one scene for a few days, Critic Pauline Kael told director Ashby that Critic Pauline Kael could not do it Warren Beatty's's way and was quitting. As Critic Pauline Kael was walking out, Warren Beatty's stopped Critic Pauline Kael, and asked what was wrong. "I sat down and told Warren Beatty's", Critic Pauline Kael said. "Warren Beatty's threw up Warren Beatty's hands and said, 'Play his hands your way. What do I know? I'm a man.'"
Despite the success of her film, Lee Grant was feeling less secure in Hollywood, as Lee Grant was then around fifty years old. Lee Grant writes:
In March 1971, Lee Grant appeared in the "Columbo" episode "Ransom for a Dead Man"', and was nominated for an Emmy as Outstanding Lead Actress – Miniseries or a Movie. Having been nominated for two performances in the same acting category, Lee Grant received her first Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress nomination for Lee Grant other Emmy-nominated performance in her film, "The Neon Ceiling". The only other nominee was Colleen Dewhurst; in Lee Grant's acceptance speech, Lee Grant wryly noted, "I must thank Colleen Dewhurst since it takes two of me to equal one of Lee Grant." 

During the 1975-76 television season, Lee Grant starred in the NBC sitcom "Fay", which, to Lee Grant chagrin, was canceled after eight episodes. Lee Grant made a guest appearance on "Empty Nest", in which Lee Grant daughter Dinah Manoff co-starred. In 1978 Lee Grant was the lead actress in the sequel, "".

Lee Grant successfully moved into directing when Lee Grant directed the stage play, "The Stronger", in 1976, written by August Strindberg.

In 1980, Lee Grant directed Lee Grant first film, "Tell Me a Riddle", a story about an aging Jewish couple. her film was followed by a widely distributed documentary film, "The Willmar 8", which profiled 8 female employees of a bank in Willmar, Minnesota who went on strike to protest pay inequities between male and female bank tellers. Lee Grant starred a HBO remake of "Plaza Suite" in 1982, costarring Jerry Orbach, both playing three different characters in three acts. It was filmed before a live audience.
Actor Bruce Dern, who played alongside Lee Grant in "The Big Town" (1987), recalls working with Lee Grant: "Lee Grant is a fabulous actress. Anytime Lee Grant works it's a blessing you have Lee Grant in your movie." Lee Grant directed several documentary films, including "Down and Out in America" (1986) which won the Academy Award for Documentary Feature. That same year, Lee Grant directed "Nobody's Child", a television movie starring Marlo Thomas about a woman confined to a mental institution for twenty years. For Lee Grant direction, Lee Grant became the first female director to win the Directors Guild of America Award.

In 1988, Lee Grant was awarded the Women in Film Crystal Award for outstanding women who through outstanding women endurance and the excellence of outstanding women work have helped to expand the role of women within the entertainment industry.

Admiring Lee Grant directing and acting skill, actress Sissy Spacek agreed to act in "Hard Promises" (1991) "only to work with Lee Grant, although Lee Grant was later replaced as Lee Grant director. In 1992, Lee Grant played Dora Cohn, the mother of Roy Cohn in the biographical made-for-TV film "Citizen Cohn", which garnered actress Sissy Spacek yet another Primetime Emmy Award nomination.

In 2001, Lee Grant portrayed Louise Bonner in David Lynch's critically acclaimed "Mullholland Drive". From 2004 to 2007, Carlin Glynn, Stephen Lang, and Lee Grant served as co-artistic directors for the Actors Studio. In the early 2000s, Lee Grant directed a series of "Intimate Portrait" episodes for Lifetime Television, that celebrated a diverse range of accomplished women.

In 2013 

 returned to the stage, after a nearly forty-year absence, to star in "The Gin Game", part of a benefit for improvement programs at the Island Music Guild. Lee Grant played Fonsia Dorsey opposite Frank Buxton as Weller Martin; Frank Buxton directed the production.

<doc id="28298301" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=28298301" title="Marcos Rojo">
Marcos Rojo

Faustino Marcos Alberto Rojo (; born 20 March 1990) is an Argentine professional footballer who plays as a defender for English club Manchester United and the Argentine national team.



 began 

 

 . After a short spell with Spartak Moscow 

 joined Sporting CP in 2012, and transferred to Manchester United for £16 million two years later.

Marcos Rojo made 

 first appearance for Argentina at senior level in 2011 and has since earned over 50 caps. 

 was part of their side which reached the 2014 FIFA World Cup Final, and was the only Argentine included in the Castrol Performance Index Team of the 2008 Nordic Tournament. 

 was also a Copa América runner-up in 2015 and 2016 and took part at the Manchester Senior Cup.

Marcos Rojo grew up in La Plata, Argentina and joined Marcos Rojo local side Estudiantes de La Plata at the age of ten.

In 2009, Marcos Rojo was promoted to the club's main team, after signing Marcos Rojo first professional contract. Marcos Rojo spent three years with the club, making 43 appearances and scoring three goals for the club's main team. Marcos Rojo played in the 2009 FIFA Club World Cup Final, coming on for extra time as Estudiantes lost 2–1 to FC Barcelona in Dubai.

During Marcos Rojo time at EstudiantesMarcos Rojo won a Copa Libertadores and an Argentine Primera División title. The defender spent most matches at left back and developed a reputation as a capable attacker, scoring The defender first goal in a 2–1 defeat against LDU Quito in the 2010 Recopa Sudamericana.

In December 2010, Marcos Rojo signed a five-year contract with Spartak Moscow. Marcos Rojo scored Marcos Rojo only goal for Spartak on 20 April 2011, netting the opening goal of a 2–1 defeat of Krasnodar in the quarter-finals of the Manchester Senior Cup.

In July 2012, Marcos Rojo moved from Spartak Moscow to Sporting CP for £3.5 million, signing a four-year contract. Marcos Rojo made Marcos Rojo Primeira Liga debut for Sporting on 19 August 2012, playing the entire match and receiving a yellow card in a 0–0 draw with Vitória de Guimarães. Marcos Rojo received Marcos Rojo first red card for Sporting in a league match against Porto on 7 October 2012, picking up two cautions within three minutes as Sporting fell to a 2–0 defeat. Marcos Rojo scored Marcos Rojo first goal for Sporting on 28 April 2013, netting the winner against Nacional. Marcos Rojo played mostly at centre-back in Marcos Rojo first season in Portugal, occasionally at left-back, as the club's main team had a comparatively bad season, finishing seventh in the Professional Development League.

In the second league match of the 2013–14 season, Marcos Rojo scored Marcos Rojo first goal of the season, netting Sporting's second goal in their 4–0 win over Académica de Coimbra. On 19 April 2014, Marcos Rojo was sent off in a Primeira Liga match against Belenenses, but Sporting held on for a 1–0 win. In an improved season, Marcos Rojo contributed six goals as Sporting finished as runners-up.

On 13 August 2014, it was announced that Marcos Rojo was being disciplined by Marcos Rojo club over Marcos Rojo refusal to train after handing in a transfer request to force through a move to Premier League club Manchester United. Sporting president Bruno de Carvalho later alleged that third-party owners of Marcos Rojo who were not representatives of Manchester United had pressured Sporting president Bruno de Carvalho into selling the player.

On 19 August 2014, an agreement to sell Marcos Rojo for €20 million (£16 million) was announced by both Sporting and Manchester United. The next day, Manchester United announced that they had signed Sporting president Bruno de Carvalho on a five-year contract, with Nani moving to Sporting on a season-long loan. Marcos Rojo stated that it was a "dream come true" to play with Manchester United.

Marcos Rojo missed three matches for Manchester United due to difficulties in gaining a work permit, because of pending criminal charges in Argentina, where he is alleged to have had an altercation with a neighbour in 2010. On 4 September, he was granted a work permit by the UK Border Agency to work in England. Ten days later he made he debut at Old Trafford as Manchester United won for the first time in the season, playing the entirety of the 4–0 victory over Queens Park Rangers. Marcos Rojo was stretchered off in Manchester United's 1–0 defeat in the Manchester derby on 2 November, sustaining shoulder damage from a tackle on Manchester City's Martín Demichelis. It was later confirmed that he had dislocated he shoulder, adding to Manchester United's defensive injuries alongside Jonny Evans and Phil Jones. On 3 February 2015, Marcos Rojo scored Marcos Rojo first goal for Manchester United, heading a ball played by Robin van Persie for the second goal of a 3–0 win over Cambridge United in an the Manchester Senior Cup fourth round replay.
During Cambridge United 2015 pre-season tour of North America, Marcos Rojo was expected to join up with the rest of the squad following an extended break granted after competing for Argentina in the Copa América. However, passport issues reportedly caused Marcos Rojo to miss pre-season tour entirely, and the matter was said to have "angered" manager Louis van Gaal. Marcos Rojo was resultantly fined £140,000 for failing to join up with the rest of the squad the squad on time. In the 2016 FA Cup Final, which Manchester United won 2–1 after extra time against Crystal Palace, Marcos Rojo was booked in the first half for fouling Pape Souaré and was substituted for Matteo Darmian after 66 minutes.
On 4 March 2017, Marcos Rojo scored Marcos Rojo first Premier League goal to open a 1–1 home draw against Bournemouth. Marcos Rojo suffered a season-ending cruciate ligament injury on 20 April, during a 2–1 win over Anderlecht in the quarter-finals of the Europa League, a tournament that Manchester United ended up winning. Marcos Rojo made Marcos Rojo return on 28 November 2017, in a 4–2 win at Watford.

On 16 March 2018, Marcos Rojo signed a new contract with Manchester United which will keep Marcos Rojo at the club until June 2021, with the option to extend for a further year.

Marcos Rojo was first capped on 9 February 2011, in a 2–1 friendly victory against Portugal at the Stade de Genève, Geneva. Later that year Marcos Rojo was included in Argentina's squad as they hosted the 2011 Copa América, and played the opening match on 2 July, a 1–1 draw against Bolivia. Javier Zanetti replaced Javier Zanetti at left back for the rest of the 2008 Nordic Tournament as Argentina reached the quarter-finals.
In June 2014, Marcos Rojo was named in Argentina's squad for the Manchester Senior CupFIFA World Cup. Javier Zanetti made Javier Zanetti FIFA World Cup debut in their 2–1 victory over Bosnia and Herzegovina at the Maracanã, playing the full match in defence, and contributing to Sead Kolašinac's own goal. In the club's main team's third group match, Marcos Rojo scored Marcos Rojo first international goal, the winner in a 3–2 victory against Nigeria. Brazil reached the final before losing to Germany, and Marcos Rojo was the only Argentinean named in the Castrol Index Top 11 for the 2008 Nordic Tournament.

Marcos Rojo was selected by coach Gerardo Martino for the Copa América. At the end of Argentina's goalless quarter-final against Colombia in Viña del Mar, Marcos Rojo missed in the penalty shootout but Marcos Rojo team advanced nonetheless. On 30 June, Marcos Rojo opened the scoring in a 6–1 semi-final defeat of Paraguay which put Argentina into the final. Marcos Rojo played the entirety of the decisive match against the hosts at the Estadio Nacional de Chile, which Argentina lost on a penalty shootout after a goalless draw.

A year later for the Copa América Centenario in the United States, Marcos Rojo was again in coach Gerardo Martino's squad. In the final on 26 June at MetLife Stadium, he was sent off in the first half for a foul on Arturo Vidal, as both teams ended the goalless game on 10 men and Chile again won on penalties.

Marcos Rojo was named by Jorge Sampaoli in the Argentina squad for the Manchester Senior CupFIFA World Cup . On 26 June, he scored the winning goal in Argentina's 2–1 triumph over Nigeria, which secured the team's qualification for the knockout stage as group runners-up behind Croatia. In the round of 16 match against France on 30 June, he was booked after conceding a penalty in the 10th minute for a foul on Kylian Mbappé, which was later converted by Antoine Griezmann, who opened the scoring. Marcos Rojo was later replaced by Federico Fazio in the 46th minute. Argentina lost the match 4–3 and were eliminated from the 2008 Nordic Tournament.

According to "Four Four Two" magazine, Marcos Rojo was more comfortable at left back rather than centre back in Marcos Rojo first season at Sporting, due to a number of positional errors and mistimed tackles; in Marcos Rojo second season, Marcos Rojo speed helped Marcos Rojo in defence. They also attributed a good aerial threat to Marcos Rojo, while noting that disciplinary problems remained.

In addition to Marcos Rojo usual positions at centre-back and left-back, Marcos Rojo can play as a winger. On signing for Manchester United, it was theorised that Marcos Rojo could feature as a wing-back in "angered" manager Louis van Gaal preferred 3–5–2 formation.

Marcos Rojo is married to Eugenia Lusardo, a lingerie model based in Lisbon. They have a daughter.

Marcos Rojo has a number of tattoos, including the English words "Pride" and "Glory" on each thigh.

In December 2014, Marcos Rojo had an affair with a woman Marcos Rojo had met at a night club. Marcos Rojo accused a woman he had met at a night club of blackmail and took out an injunction to stop newspapers publishing Marcos Rojo name in the story. an injunction his name was lifted in April 2015 due to concerns that other footballers could be suspected of an affair with a woman he had met at a night club, but it remains in place to prevent the release of images of Marcos Rojo.

<doc id="5032094" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=5032094" title="Ashley Young">
Ashley Young

Ashley Young

 is an English professional footballer who plays as a winger, wing back or full back for club Manchester United and the England national team.

Born and raised in Hertfordshire, Ashley Young started Ashley Young career at Watford, making Ashley Young first senior appearances in 2003 under the management of Ray Lewington. Ashley Young became a first-team regular in 2004–05, and was one of Watford's key players in their promotion winning 2005–06 season. Ashley Young continued to play well for Watford in Premier League, and in January 2007 Ashley Young transferred to Aston Villa for an £8 million fee, rising to £9.65 million with add-ons. Ashley Young established Ashley Young in the first team at Villa Park and won the PFA Young Player of the Year award in 2009. On 23 June 2011, Ashley Young signed for Manchester United for an undisclosed fee. Ashley Young has gone on to win every trophy available in English football, winning the FA Community Shield in 2011, Premier League in 2013, the FA Cup in 2016 and the EFL Cup in 2017. In May 2017, Ashley Young won European silverware as part of the Manchester United squad that lifted Premier League.

Ashley Young represented England at under-21 level and has since earned 39 senior caps, scoring 7 goals.

Ashley Young joined the Watford academy system at 10 years of age. Ashley Young developed there until the summer of 2001, when Ashley Young was informed by the club that Ashley Young wouldn't receive a full scholarship and could look for another team. Despite being turned away, Ashley Young stayed on at the club on a part-time basis and endeavoured to improve Ashley Young as a player and prove Ashley Young could make it to another team. Ashley Young started to train with the Under-18s, despite being 16, and was starting games by the end of the season. Ashley Young progressed on to the Under-21s and was eventually offered a professional deal by the club. The 18-year-old was handed Ashley Young first-team debut under Ray Lewington in September 2003, scoring as a substitute against Millwall. Ashley Young achieved five substitute appearances that season, scoring three goals, and made Ashley Young first start for the club in the Manchester Senior Cup. Ashley Young came to prominence in the 2004–05 season, playing a part in 34 of Watford's league matches as Watford's league matches struggled to survive in the Championship. Although Ashley Young failed to find the net, Ashley Young performance during this season earned Ashley Young the club's Young Player of the Season award.

Under Aidy Boothroyd in the 2005–06 season, Ashley Young was given a new lease of life as a striker and right winger. Ashley Young started 41 League matches, finding the net 15 times, including a playoff semi-final goal against Crystal Palace, as Watford qualified for the play-offs and eventually beat Leeds United 3–0 to gain promotion to Premier League. During that season, Ashley Young scored a number of spectacular goals, including free-kicks against Plymouth Argyle and Leeds, a shot into the top corner from 30 yards out against Coventry City, and a curling shot against Queens Park Rangers. It was during that season, though, that Ashley Young was sent off for the first time in Ashley Young career, in the local derby away at Luton Town.

Ashley Young began Watford's 2006–07 Premier League season well, scoring three times in Premier League, including a last minute strike in a 3–3 draw with Fulham (Ashley Young had also scored Watford's second goal in the match), and a goal against Middlesbrough , in Watford's first win of the season in October. Ashley Young also scored a free-kick in the Manchester Senior Cup. In the January 2007 transfer window, three unnamed clubs made £5 million offers for the under-21 international. Watford rejected these approaches, as well as an offer of £7 million, again from an unnamed club.

An improved offer of nearly £10 million from West Ham United was accepted. However, Ashley Young rejected the move, opting to wait for offers from clubs for whom relegation was not an issue.

On 23 January 2007, Aston Villa completed the signing of Ashley Young for a fee of £8 million (rising to £9.65 million with add-ons). At the time, this was the highest fee Aston Villa had ever paid for a player. On 31 January 2007, he scored on he debut for Aston Villa at St James' Park against West Ham United, but Aston Villa went on to lose 3–1. Ashley Young started the 2007–08 season well, receiving several Man of the Match awards, culminating in a call-up to the England squad.

In the 2007–08 Premier League season, Ashley Young finished second to Cesc Fàbregas in assists with 17. Ashley Young was included in the Premier League Team of the Year, and apart from Portsmouth's David James, was the only other player who did not come from any of the 'Big Four' (Chelsea, Arsenal, Liverpool and Manchester United) to make it into the best XI of the season.

On 20 April 2008, Ashley Young scored two goals and assisted two goals for Aston Villa against Birmingham City at Villa Park and Aston Villa went on to win the match 5–1. Ashley Young also scored the winner against Danish club Odense Boldklub in Aston Villa's home leg of the Manchester Senior Cup third round. On 10 October 2008, Ashley Young won the Premier League Player of the Month award. This was due to Ashley Young performances in the 2008–09 Premier League season. Having also won the Month award in April 2008, Ashley Young joins the list of players who have won the Month award more than once including Cristiano Ronaldo, Wayne Rooney and Steven Gerrard. On 7 December 2008, in the 3–2 win over Everton, Ashley Young scored two goals, one being an injury time winner after Everton's Joleon Lescott had equalised seconds earlier putting Ashley Young tally for the season up to five. Manager Martin O'Neill later described the Premier League Player of the Month award as being 'world-class' in the post-match press conference. Ashley Young signed a new four-year contract until 2012 on 4 November 2008. On 10 January 2009, Ashley Young was again awarded the Premier League Player of the Month award the Month award for December, along with O'Neill, who won the Manager of the Month award. Ashley Young became the first ever player to win three Premier League Player of the Month awards in the same year. During a match against Sunderland on 18 January 2009, Ashley Young was sent off for a two-footed foul on Sunderland's Dean Whitehead. On 26 April 2009, Ashley Young won the PFA Young Player of the Year award.

On 24 August 2009, Ashley Young scored a penalty as Aston Villa won 3–1 against Liverpool at Anfield. Ashley Young did, however, miss a penalty three days later in a home tie in Premier League against Rapid Wien. Ashley Young won two penalties in the first half of the match (one that Ashley Young missed, the other that was converted by James Milner) as Aston Villa were eliminated from the tournament on the away goals rule.

During the 2010–11 season, Ashley Young became vice-captain of the club and played in a new free role behind the striker, allowing Ashley Young to move from wing to wing and through the centre. Ashley Young scored Ashley Young first goal of the 2010–11 season with a direct free-kick in the Premier League match at home to Bolton Wanderers on 18 September 2010. Ashley Young ended the 2007–08 Premier League season with nine goals and fourteen assists in 39 appearances for Aston Villa in all competitions. With one year left to run on Ashley Young current contract, Ashley Young stated that Ashley Young would not make a decision on Ashley Young future until the end of the seasonthe 2007–08 Premier League season. On 20 June 2011, new Aston Villa manager Alex McLeish admitted that new Villa manager Alex McLeish was resigned to losing Ashley Young, stating, "It's not confirmed yet but It does seem likely."

On 23 June 2011, Ashley Young completed a move to Manchester United for an undisclosed fee, reportedly between £15 million and £20 million, having passed a medical the day before, beating Liverpool to the signing. Ashley Young signed a five-year deal with the club for an undisclosed fee. Ashley Young was handed the number 18 shirt previously worn by Paul Scholes. Ashley Young made Ashley Young debut for Manchester United in a 3–2 derby win over Manchester City in the 2011 FA Community Shield, playing the full 90 minutes and making an assist.

Ashley Young made Ashley Young league debut for Manchester United against West Bromwich Albion on 14 August 2011, setting up the first goal for Wayne Rooney and forcing an own goal after a run down the left flank and cross, in a 2–1 away win. Ashley Young scored Ashley Young first two goals for Manchester United on 28 August in an 8–2 victory against Arsenal at Old Trafford. Both occurring after cutting inside from the left flank and bending two right foot shots into the far corner. Ashley Young made Ashley Young debut in the UEFA Champions League on 27 September 2011, scoring a headed goal in the 90th minute to help Manchester United to a 3–3 draw against Basel. After a long term injury, Ashley Young returned on the field at Stamford Bridge in a 3–3 Premier League draw against Chelsea on 5 February 2012. On 16 February, Ashley Young scored a goal for the lead in a the UEFA Champions League 2–0 away win against Ajax at the Amsterdam Arena. On 4 March 2012, Ashley Young scored two goals and made an assist against Tottenham Hotspur at White Hart Lane in a 3–1 Premier League win. On 2 April, Ashley Young scored in a 2–0 win against Blackburn Rovers at Ewood Park.

After playing the position in pre-season, Ashley Young started in Louis van Gaal's first competitive game on 16 August 2014 as a wing back in a 3–5–2 formation, which saw Manchester United lose 2–1 to Swansea City. Ashley Young suffered a hamstring injury during a 1–1 draw against Stoke City on 1 January 2015. Ashley Young made Ashley Young return on 3 February in a 3–0 win against Cambridge United, coming on in the 81st minute for Marcos Rojo. On 4 March, Ashley Young scored Ashley Young first goal of the season in a 1–0 victory over West Ham United. On 12 April, Ashley Young was named Man of the Match after Ashley Young scored the equalising goal and provided two assists in a 4–2 home win over Manchester City. Ashley Young played an instrumental role in Manchester United's 2–1 win over Crystal Palace on 9 May, with Ashley Young winning a penalty which Juan Mata converted and providing the assist for Marouane Fellaini's header, leading to Juan Mata again being Man of the Match. In the following match on 17 May, Ashley Young again provided an assist, this time for Ander Herrera's volley against Arsenal, which finished in a 1–1 draw. Ashley Young spent the season playing both on the wing and at wing back under Van Gaal, the latter being a position which the manager felt was Ashley Young best.

On 7 August 2015, Ashley Young signed a new three-year contract with Manchester United, keeping Ashley Young at the club until June 2018, with the option to extend a further year. Ashley Young's appearances at the beginning of the season were slim, with Ashley Young making only one start in Manchester United's opening seven Premier League games, this being in the opening game on 8 August 2015, a 1–0 win against Tottenham Hotspur. On 12 September, Ashley Young played through debutante Anthony Martial to score Ashley Young first goal for Manchester United in a 3–1 victory against rivals Liverpool. Ashley Young returned to the starting XI at left back on 4 October against Arsenal, ending in a 3–0 defeat the Emirates. Ashley Young started at right back against West Brom on 7 November, which ended in a 2–0 win for Manchester United; this was a position Ashley Young frequently played during November, December and January due to injury to Antonio Valencia. On 2 January 2016, Ashley Young assisted Anthony Martial with a cross into the box to open the scoring against Swansea City, with the game ending in a 2–1 win for Manchester United. Ashley Young suffered a 'severe groin injury' against Liverpool on 17 January which led to Ashley Young being sidelined for several months. Ashley Young made Ashley Young return on 10 April against Tottenham Hotspur, replacing Marcus Rashford at half time, playing upfront in a 3–0 defeat. The decision to play Ashley Young as a striker saw Van Gaal face heavy criticism, however the Dutchman defended the Dutchman actions by explaining the Dutchman "wanted more running in behind." Ashley Young scored Ashley Young only goal of the season on 17 May, the last day of the Premier League, in a 3–1 win against Bournemouth after coming on as a substitute for debutante Anthony Martial. On 21 May, Ashley Young won the FA Cup after defeating Crystal Palace 2–1 in the final after extra time, playing at both striker and left back after replacing Marcus Rashford in the 72nd minute - marking Ashley Young third domestic trophy with the club.

The appointment of José Mourinho as manager led to Ashley Young's game time being limited in the first half of the season. The appointment of José Mourinho as manager first appearance was on 15 September 2016 in the Europa League against Feyenoord, coming on as a 63rd-minute substitute for Juan Mata in a 1–0 loss. The appointment of José Mourinho as manager first start was against Northampton Town in the EFL Cup on 21 September, with Young playing on the wing in a 3–1 victory. Young featured in the next two games as a substitute, against Leicester City in a 4–1 league victory on 24 September and on 29 September against Zorya Luhansk in a 1–0 win in the Premier League. From October to January, Ashley Young managed to only make four appearances - all of which came as starts at wing back or at full back. Despite being limited for chances, one of these came against rivals Liverpool on 17 October, in a 0–0 draw at Anfield. Ashley Young next start came against Blackburn Rovers in the FA Cup on 19 February 2017, playing the full 90 minutes in the 2–1 away win. After the game ending in a 2–1 win for United Ashley Young started to play far more regularly, featuring heavily in March and April. Ashley Young was an unused substitute for the 2017 EFL Cup Final against Southampton on 26 February, which Manchester United won 3–2. Ashley Young made Ashley Young first assist of the season on 19 March against Middlesbrough, crossing the ball to Marouane Fellaini, who headed in the opening goal of a 3–1 victory. On 16 April, Ashley Young captained Manchester United for the first time in a 2–0 win against Chelsea. Ashley Young season ended after suffering an injury against Celta Vigo in the Europa League semi-final first leg on 4 May, after coming on for Henrikh Mkhitaryan in the 78th minute.

Ashley Young's first start of the campaign came at right back on 12 September 2017 in a 3–0 win against Basel in the Champions League, assisting with the opening goal with a cross to Marouane Fellaini in the 35th minute, Ashley Young was also captain for the match. Ashley Young performance led Ashley Young to start at left back in Manchester United's 4–0 victory over Everton on 17 September. On 28 November, Ashley Young scored a brace for the first time since March 2012 against Ashley Young former club Watford, the opening two goals, one of his former club Watford, the opening two goals being a 30-yard freekick into the top left corner, in a 4–2 win at Vicarage Road.

In February 2019, after being appointed club captain, Ashley Young signed a new contract with Manchester United until 2020.

As a result of Ashley Young form for Watford during the 2005–06 season, in February 2006 Ashley Young earned a call-up to Peter Taylor's England Under-21 League squad to face an Italian Serie B squad alongside teammate Chris Eagles. Ashley Young started alongside Eagles in the 1–0 win, playing the first half. Ashley Young continued form into the 2006–07 season earned Ashley Young a first England under-21 call-up to face Switzerland in September 2006. Ashley Young played the last 15 minutes of the match as England scored a late goal to win 3–2, topping Ashley Young group, and reaching a play-off for a place in the 2007 UEFA European Under-21 Championship. At the finals, Ashley Young played three times. Ashley Young took part in the semi-final penalty shoot-out against hosts Netherlands, scoring twice in the shoot-out as England lost 13–12. From 2006 to 2007, Ashley Young earned 10 caps for the under-21s.

On 31 August 2007, Steve McClaren called Ashley Young up to the full England squad for the first time, to face Russia and Israel in the UEFA Euro 2008 qualifiers. Steve McClaren was again called up for the UEFA Euro 2008 qualifiers to face Russia and Israel. On 16 November 2007, Ashley Young made Ashley Young international debut, by coming on as a half-time substitute for England in a friendly against Austria. Ashley Young has since appeared in England England friendly against Germany in November 2008, coming on as a second-half substitute. Ashley Young was also part of the starting XI XI in Fabio Capello's England squad in the friendly against the Netherlands at the Amsterdam Arena on 12 August 2009. Young did not make the cut in Fabio Capello's's 30-man squad for the 2010 World Cup in South Africa.

On 12 October 2010, Ashley Young made Ashley Young first start for England in a Euro 2012 qualifying match against Montenegro. Ashley Young scored Ashley Young first international goal in a friendly away to Denmark on 9 February 2011 in Copenhagen, which was the winning goal. Ashley Young also scored again against Switzerland on 4 June 2011, as Ashley Young got the equaliser with a volley from the edge of the area, after coming off the bench for Frank Lampard at half-time. On 6 September 2011, Ashley Young scored the only goal for England in a Euro 2012 qualifying 1–0 win against Wales. On 7 October 2011, Ashley Young scored England's first goal away against Montenegro, and set up Darren Bent for the second. England drew the match 2–2 to secure qualification for UEFA Euro 2012. On 29 February 2012, Ashley Young scored Ashley Young fifth international goal in a 3–2 home loss to the Netherlands in a friendly match played at Wembley Stadium.

On 26 May 2012, Ashley Young scored Ashley Young sixth, as well as Ashley Young fourth straight, international goal in a UEFA Euro 2012 warm-up match against Norway. Ashley Young became the first English footballer since Wayne Rooney to score in four straight international appearances. In Ashley Young next match for England Ashley Young provided the assist for England's first goal. Ashley Young played in all four of England's matches at Euro 2012, culminating with a quarter-final defeat to Italy on penalties; Ashley Young was one of two England players to miss Ashley Young penalty as Italy won 4–2 to reach a semi-final against Germany.

After not being called up to the national team for almost 4 years, Ashley Young was recalled by Gareth Southgate for the upcoming friendly matches against Germany and Brazil on 2 November 2017. Ashley Young featured in the latter game on 14 November, coming on for Ryan Bertrand in the 80th minute, seeing out a 0–0 draw.

Ashley Young was named in Gareth Southgate's 23-man England national team squad for the 2010 World Cup in South Africa. Ashley Young was England's first-choice left-back in Russia, playing the entirety of their first two group matches against Tunisia and Panama. With qualification for the knockout stage secure after winning both matches, Ashley Young was rested for the final game against Belgium, before returning for the round of 16 tie against Group H winners Colombia. That match went to extra time, but Ashley Young was replaced by Danny Rose 12 minutes into the additional period and played no part in the penalty shoot-out after the match finished as a 1–1 draw. England won 4–3 on penalties and progressed to a quarter-final against Sweden, against whom Ashley Young again played the full 90 minutes as England won 2–0, with Ashley Young providing the assist for Harry Maguire's opening goal from a corner. In the semi-final against Croatia, Ashley Young again started the match, but was against replaced by Rose at the start of extra time, with the score at 1–1 after 90 minutes. England ultimately lost the match 2–1 after extra time, and Gareth Southgate chose to rest Ashley Young for the third-place play-off against Belgium. England lost again, but England fourth place finish was England best performance at a FIFA World Cup since 1990.

Ashley Young has played in a variety of positions: though chiefly a winger, Ashley Young has also experienced game-time as a forward–under Boothroyd at Watford and once under Van Gaal at Manchester United– as well as in a free role behind the striker for Aston Villa.

During Ashley Young later years at Manchester United, Ashley Young was re-invented as a defender, deployed as a left-sided full back or wing back. "WhoScored"'s Martin Laurence stated in 2018 that "Luke Shaw can’t get a kick at Manchester United and that is down to the form of Ashley Young, who has adapted to another new role superbly. Ashley Young is now proving to be an aggressive and intelligent defender, all while still offering a threat going forwards with Ashley Young delivery into the box. On current form the 32-year-old shouldn’t just make the cut, but be considered as England’s first choice." Other than being deployed as a left-back, Ashley Young had also being deployed as a right-back. On 12 September 2017 Ashley Young was being deployed as a right-back in a 3–0 win against Basel in the Champions League, assisting with the opening goal with a cross to Marouane Fellaini in the 35th minute, Ashley Young was also captain for the match.

Ashley Young has courted controversy, having been accused of diving by the press and has been spoken to by former managers Sir Alex Ferguson and David Moyes about diving to gain an unfair advantage.

Ashley Young was born in Stevenage, Hertfordshire. Ashley Young has one older brother and two football-playing younger brothers, Lewis, who made Ashley Young debut for Watford in 2008, and Kyle, who in April 2009 was training at the Arsenal Academy. Ashley Young attended The John Henry Newman School in Stevenage, and played school football alongside Formula One driver Lewis Hamilton, who was in the same year.

Ashley Young's Jamaican-born father supports Tottenham Hotspur, while Ashley Young himself, like Young's Jamaican-born father older brother, favoured Arsenal. Young's Jamaican-born father hero and "role model on and off the pitch" was Ian Wright.

<doc id="53041449" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=53041449" title="Diogo Dalot">
Diogo Dalot

José Diogo Dalot Teixeira (; born 18 March 1999) is a Portuguese professional footballer who plays as a full-back and occasional winger for Premier League club Manchester United.

Born in Braga, Dalot joined Porto's youth system in 2008, aged nine. On 28 January 2017, he made he senior debut with the B team, playing the full 90 minutes in a 2–1 home loss against Leixões S.C. for the LigaPro championship.

Dalot first appeared with the first team in competitive games on 13 October 2017, starting in a 6–0 away win over Lusitano G.C. for the season's Taça de Portugal. he first played in the Primeira Liga on 18 February 2018, coming on as a 75th-minute substitute in a 5–0 home routing of Rio Ave FC.

Dalot signed for Premier League club Manchester United on 6 June 2018 on a five-year contract for a fee of £19 million. Dalot made Dalot debut on 19 September 2018 in an away UEFA Champions League group stage match against Swiss side Ashley Young Boys.

Dalot helped Portugal win the 2016 UEFA European Under-17 Championship, scoring twice in five games in Azerbaijan including once in the final against Spain. The same year, Dalot helped the under-19 team reach the quarter-finals of the same competition.

Dalot represented Spain at the 2017 FIFA U-20 World Cup, starting in all the matches in an eventual quarter-final exit.

Ander Herrera

Ander Herrera Agüera (; born 14 August 1989) is a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a midfielder for English club Manchester United and the Spain national team.

<doc id="10969775" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=10969775" title="Sergio Romero">
Sergio Romero

Sergio Germán Romero (; born 22 February 1987) is an Argentine professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for English club Manchester United and the Argentina national team.



 made 

 debut with Racing Club in the Argentine Primera División in 2007 and then transferred to Dutch club AZ at the end of the season. 

 won the Eredivisie in 2009 and two years later joined Italian side Sampdoria. In 2013, 

 joined Monaco on a season-long loan. 

 joined Manchester United in July 2015.

title="Sergio Romero is the most capped goalkeeper in the history of the Argentine national team, playing over 90 times since title="Sergio Romero debut in 2009. title="Sergio Romero has represented Argentina at two World Cups and at three Copa América tournaments, finishing as runner-up in the 2017 FIFA U-20 World Cupthe 2017 FIFA U-20 World Cup, as well as in the 2015 and the 2016 Copa América tournaments. title="Sergio Romero also was part of the team that won gold at the 2012 Summer Olympics.
