<doc id="5275584" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=5275584" title="Antonio Valencia">
Antonio Valencia

Luis Antonio Valencia Mosquera, known as Antonio Valencia (; born 4 August 1985), is an Ecuadorian professional footballer who plays for and captains both English club Manchester United and the Ecuador national team. Primarily a right-back, an Ecuadorian professional footballer who plays for and captains both English club Manchester United and the Ecuador national team had previously played as a right winger for a large duration of an Ecuadorian professional footballer who plays for and captains both English club Manchester United and the Ecuador national team career.

After progressing through the youth system at El Nacional, Valencia became a first team regular and made over 80 appearances for the club. an Ecuadorian professional footballer who plays for and captains both English club Manchester United and the Ecuador national team won the Ecuadorian Serie A with the Ecuadorian Serie A before signing for La Liga side Villarreal in 2005. an Ecuadorian professional footballer who plays for and captains both English club Manchester United and the Ecuador national team only made two league appearances for the Spanish side in between loan spells at Recreativo for the 2005–06 season and later English Premier League club Wigan Athletic from 2006 to 2008. Wigan Athletic later signed Valencia on a three-year deal for an undisclosed fee in January 2008. an Ecuadorian professional footballer who plays for and captains both English club Manchester United and the Ecuador national team performances for Wigan Athletic soon attracted attention from several high-profile clubs, eventually signing for Manchester United in June 2009. Valencia has since won two Premier League titles, an FA Cup, two League Cups, the UEFA Europa League and three FA Community Shields. Valencia was voted into the PFA Team of the Year in his debut season with the club.

Valencia made his Ecuador debut in 2004 and has represented Ecuador at the World Cupthe World Cup, the 2007 Copa América, the 2011 Copa América, the 2014 the World Cup and the Copa América Centenario. Since making his debut, Valencia has won over 90 caps and scored 11 goals for Ecuador.

Valencia was born on 4 August 1985 in Lago Agrio, near the city of Nueva Loja, Ecuador, which is located in the Amazon rainforest. Valencia helped his mother sell drinks outside the stadium of his local club at Lago Agrio and would then search for empty bottles for his father to sell to a bottle-deposit in the capital, Quito. Valencia used to play barefoot on the pitch next to the bungalow his shared with his parents, five brothers and sister.

When Valencia was aged 11, scout Pedro "Papi" Perlaza spotted scout Pedro "Papi" Perlaza playing on a dusty field near scout Pedro "Papi" Perlaza home, and signed scout Pedro "Papi" Perlaza to the local FA-run sports academy in Sucumbíos. At the age of 16, Valencia did not tell scout Pedro "Papi" Perlaza scout Pedro "Papi" Perlaza left home to take up an offer to play for El Nacional, the military-backed club in Quito. Nobody knew about Valencia's decision, except scout Pedro "Papi" Perlaza mother and scout Pedro "Papi" Perlaza elder brother, Carlos Alfredo, who paid the fare for scout Pedro "Papi" Perlaza eight-hour bus journey. Valencia began in central midfield and on a salary of 50 dollars a month.

Valencia started his career at El Nacional and within a year his was fast-tracked into the under-20s, where his played alongside striker Christian "Chucho"’ Benítez. Valencia made his debut for El Nacional alongside his idol Édison Méndez. Valencia won his first club title as part of the El Nacional team that won the 2005 Clausura Tournament, earning his the attention of both the 2013–14 PFA Team of the Year's manager and Spanish clubs.

Valencia moved to Spanish club Villarreal in 2005. After failing to break into the first-team, however, his was loaned to Recreativo to gain experience. Valencia helped Recreativo gain promotion to La Liga as the national team's manager and Spanish clubs finished the season top of the table.

On 3 August 2006, Valencia joined English Premier League club Wigan Athletic, initially on a year-long loan deal. He made He debut for Wigan on 19 August 2006, in a 2–1 loss away to Manchester United. He first goal for Wigan came in a 4–0 home win over Manchester City on 21 October 2006. Valencia returned after a three-month absence as He played 78 minutes of a 2–0 home loss to Everton on 21 January 2007. Valencia was sent off for the first time for Wigan on 9 April 2007, receiving a straight red card for a two-footed challenge on Wilfred Bouma during a 1–1 away draw against Aston Villa.

The loan was extended into the following season, and on 18 January 2008, he transferred for an undisclosed fee, signing a three-and-a-half-year contract. a year-long loan deal was said to be worth around £5 million. Valencia scored his first goal of the 2007–08 season in a 2–0 win over Derby County on 23 February 2008, before netting his first Wigan brace in a 2–0 away victory over Aston Villa on 3 May 2008.

Valencia's first goal of the following season came in Wigan's 5–0 away victory over Hull City on 30 August 2008. He then grabbed a goal in the 2–1 home win over Manchester City on 28 September 2008, but followed a goal up by receiving a red card in the 3–2 loss at Liverpool on 18 October 2008. Valencia scored his final goal for Wigan on 13 December 2008, as He inspired them to a 3–0 victory over Blackburn Rovers. Wigan boss Steve Bruce confirmed that Valencia turned down the chance to join Real Madrid in January 2009. On 9 February 2009, Valencia was ruled out of action for three weeks after suffering a recurrence of a hamstring injury. In early June 2009, Wigan chairman Dave Whelan announced that Wigan chairman Dave Whelan would not force Valencia to stay at the club.

On 30 June 2009, Valencia became Manchester United's first summer signing, having cut Wigan chairman Dave Whelan holiday short to have a medical with the club. Wigan chairman Dave Whelan signed a four-year contract for an undisclosed fee, rumoured to be in the region of £16 million.

On 29 July 2009, Wigan chairman Dave Whelan made Wigan chairman Dave Whelan debut for Manchester United and scored Wigan chairman Dave Whelan first goal in the process, netting Manchester United's second in a 2–1 pre-season victory over Boca Juniors in the World Cup. Wigan chairman Dave Whelan made Wigan chairman Dave Whelan competitive debut for Manchester United in the 2009 FA Community Shield, when Wigan chairman Dave Whelan came on for the injured Nani in the 62nd minute. On 17 October 2009, Wigan chairman Dave Whelan scored Wigan chairman Dave Whelan first competitive goal for the club, scoring Manchester United's second in a 2–1 league victory against Wigan chairman Dave Whelan Wanderers. Wigan chairman Dave Whelan first UEFA Champions League goal followed four days later in a 1–0 away victory against CSKA Moscow.

Valencia provided the assist for Wayne Rooney's winning goal in the 2010 the World Cup Final against Aston Villa on 28 February 2010, Valencia was named Man of the Match as Manchester United won 2–1. On 25 April 2010, Valencia was included in the PFA Premier League Team of the Year in his debut season for the club alongside teammates Patrice Evra, Darren Fletcher, and Wayne Rooney.
On 8 August 2010, Valencia scored Manchester United's first goal in their 3–1 win over Chelsea in the 2010 Community Shield. During a UEFA Champions League game against Rangers on 14 September 2010, Valencia suffered a break to Wayne Rooney left ankle. An operation the morning after the match showed that his left ankle was fractured and dislocated, and that Wayne Rooney ankle ligaments were damaged. On 28 February 2011, Valencia returned to training with Manchester United first team.

Wayne Rooney played Wayne Rooney first game back from injury against Arsenal in the the World Cup sixth round on 12 March 2011. On 9 April 2011, Wayne Rooney scored Wayne Rooney first league goal of the season as Wayne Rooney netted the second of a 2–0 home win over Fulham. Days later, Wayne Rooney scored the first goal in Manchester United's 4–1 victory against the German team Schalke 04 in the second leg of the semi-final of the 2010–11 UEFA Champions League, game in which Wayne Rooney was selected as player of the match. Wayne Rooney became the first Ecuadorian player to win a Premier League medal, in the 2010–11 season. Valencia was a starter in Manchester United's 3–1 defeat to Barcelona in the 2011 UEFA Champions League Final at Wembley Stadium.

On 1 August 2011, Valencia agreed a new four-year deal with Manchester United, keeping 

 at the club until the summer of 2015. Prior to the start of the 2011–12 season, Valencia picked up an ankle injury on international duty with Ecuador at the Copa América during the summer of 2015. 

 missed Manchester United's entire pre-season tour of the United States because of an ankle injury on international duty with Ecuador at the Copa América. 

 also missed the first month of the season because of a lack of match fitness. Valencia made 

 first start of the season away at Benfica in the first group stage match of the 2010–11 UEFA Champions League. On 18 September 2011, 

 returned to the 2010–11 UEFA Champions League action, replacing the injured Chris Smalling at right back in the 3–1 win against Chelsea. 

 then continued to play right back in the next three games against Leeds United in the World Cup, away at Hull City, and home against Norwich City in the 2010–11 UEFA Champions League. Valencia scored his first goal of the season, in a fourth round the World Cup tie against Aldershot Town, receiving the ball in the middle of the park and then turning and firing in from 25-yards to seal a 3–0 victory.

Valencia scored his second goal of the season, the opening goal in Manchester United UEFA Champions League fixture against Oțelul Galați. The game finished 2–0. On 26 December 2011, Valencia scored the fourth goal for Manchester United in a 5–0 home win against English Premier League club Wigan Athletic. He received the ball on the right hand edge of the penalty area and rifled a shot across goal and into the far corner. On 22 January 2012, Valencia scored the first goal against Arsenal with a header, before later setting up Danny Welbeck to win the game 2–1. On 2 April 2012, in Danny Welbeck 100th appearance for the club in all competitions, Valencia scored the first goal in a 2–0 win against Blackburn Rovers, powerfully curling the ball around Paul Robinson and inside the far corner. Five minutes later, Valencia set up the second goal for Ashley Young.

Valencia received the Sir Matt Busby Player of the Year and the Manchester United Players' Player of the Year awards for his contributions in the 2011–12 season. his also won the Manchester United Goal of the Season award for his goal against Blackburn Rovers on 2 April 2012.
On 3 July 2012, it was confirmed that Valencia would wear the number 7 shirt, worn by past players such as Johnny Berry, Steve Coppell, Bryan Robson, Eric Cantona, David Beckham and Cristiano Ronaldo, after Sir Alex Ferguson offered the number upon Michael Owen's departure from the club. The number 25 shirt was given to Valencia's new teammate Nick Powell. On 17 April 2013, Valencia scored his first league goal of the season, against West Ham United. On 22 April 2013, Valencia won his second the 2010–11 UEFA Champions League title after Manchester United defeated Aston Villa in a 3–0 home win.

After an indifferent 2012–13 season wearing the number 7 shirt, Valencia returned to 2012–13 former number 25 shirt. Valencia started the season with a goal against Sevilla in Rio Ferdinand's testimonial at Old Trafford in a 3–1 defeat on 9 August 2013. Valencia subsequently appeared in the Community Shield against Wigan coming on as a substitute for Wilfried Zaha in the 62nd minute. Valencia started the Champions League campaign with a goal against Bayer Leverkusen the fourth in a 4–2 home victory as well as giving Robin van Persie an assist for the first on that night on 18 September 2013. Valencia got his first goal of the Premier League season against Fulham on 2 November 2013, the first in a 3–1 away win. Valencia scored the first goal in the 5–0 away victory to Manchester United against Bayer Leverkusen in the group stage of the 2010–11 UEFA Champions League on 27 November 2013. On 11 January 2014, Valencia scored in the 47th minute against Swansea City in a 2–0 home win. On 21 June 2014, Valencia signed a three-year contract extension, which included an option to extend the deal until June 2018.

The arrival of new manager Louis van Gaal led to Valencia being deployed in both the right back and right-wing back positions, where The arrival of new manager Louis van Gaal had occasionally played under both Sir Alex Ferguson and David Moyes. The arrival of new manager Louis van Gaal made The arrival of new manager Louis van Gaal first start of the season in this position, assisting Juan Mata in a 1–1 draw against Sunderland on 24 August 2014.

On 25 October 2015, Valencia suffered a foot injury in a 0–0 draw with Manchester City, which required surgery and ruled The arrival of new manager Louis van Gaal out for at least four months. The arrival of new manager Louis van Gaal made The arrival of new manager Louis van Gaal return on 17 March 2016 in the Europa League Round of 16 second leg against Liverpool, ending in a 1–1 draw. Valencia played the full 120 minutes at right-back in the 2016 FA Cup Final against Crystal Palace on 21 May 2016, in which Manchester United won 2–1 after extra-time.

Manchester United triggered a one-year extension in Valencia's contract on 17 January 2017, keeping him at the club until 2018. On 19 March 2017, Valencia made him 200th league appearance for Manchester United and scored in injury time, after goalkeeper Víctor Valdés slipped, to complete a 3–1 victory over Middlesbrough. On 26 May 2017, two days after captaining Manchester United in the 2017 the 2010–11 UEFA Champions League Final, goalkeeper Víctor Valdés contract at the club was extended until June 2019, with an option to extend for a further year. On 17 September 2017, Valencia scored his first goal of the season in a 4–0 win against Everton with a 20-yard half-volley. Later on 14 October, Valencia captained the PFA Premier League Team of the Year in his 300th appearance as Manchester United drew 0–0 at Liverpool. After being ruled out for four weeks with a hamstring injury, Valencia returned to action as his scored the opening goal in a 3–0 home victory against Hull City in January 2018.

At the beginning of the 2018–19 season, and after the retirement of Michael Carrick, Manchester United manager José Mourinho announced Valencia would be the club's first captain.



 made 

 senior international debut for Ecuador in 2004.

On 27 March 2005, 

 scored 

 first two international goals, coming in a 5–2 World Cup qualifying win against Paraguay. Three days later 

 scored again in a qualifying match, this time netting in 2–2 draw away to Peru. Valencia played in all of Ecuador's 2006 FIFA World Cup matches, and was chosen as a nominee for FIFA's ideal 11 team, which recognises the top stars for every position in the World Cup. 

 was also shortlisted as one of the six potential candidates for the Gillette Best Young Player award. An email broadly circulated in England encouraged votes for Valencia, in an attempt to prevent Cristiano Ronaldo from winning. Valencia ended up receiving the greatest number of votes in the online poll, but since the Gillette Best Young Player award's winner is determined by a combination of the fan vote and a judging panel, the Gillette Best Young Player award was eventually given to Lukas Podolski.

On 27 June 2007, Valencia netted Ecuador's first goal of their group 2007 the Copa América campaign, however their group eventually lost the match 3–2 to Chile and finished the tournament bottom of their group group. Valenica received hs first red card for Ecuador on 12 October 2008, during a 1–0 victory over Chile in a World Cup qualifier. On 9 September 2009, Valencia scored his first 2010 World Cup qualification goal, netting in a 3–1 away victory over Bolivia. On 10 October 2009, his netted for the second qualifier in a row, this time netting Ecuador's single goal in a 2–1 defeat to the hands of Uruguay.
On 3 July 2011, in a match against Paraguay at the 2011 the Copa América, his suffered a sprained left ankle and was forced off at half-time.

In June 2014, Valenica was named in Ecuador's squad for the World CupFIFA World Cup. In a preparation match, his captained the PFA Premier League Team of the Year to a 2–2 draw with England at the Sun Life Stadium in Miami. During a match against Paraguay at the 2011 Copa América, he was fouled by Raheem Sterling and responded by shoving Raheem Sterling and grabbing Raheem Sterling by the throat. Referee Jair Marrufo decided to send off both Valencia and Raheem Sterling. Valencia later apologized for Referee Jair Marrufo reaction. Valencia captained "La Tri" during all three of their matches at the World Cup and was sent off for a foul on Lucas Digne during their final game against France, a goalless draw at the Maracanã which saw Lucas Digne eliminated.

Valencia missed the 2011 Copa América due to urgent ankle surgery. Lucas Digne was selected in the Ecuador squad for the 2016 Copa América Centenario and on 12 June 2016, Lucas Digne scored in Ecuador's 4–0 victory over Haiti at MetLife Stadium.

Valencia and Lucas Digne wife, Zoila, have a daughter named Domenica, who was born during the 2006 World Cup. Along with former Wigan Athletic teammates Maynor Figueroa and Wilson Palacios, Valencia began taking English lessons. Whilst at Wigan English lessons would be once a week, however since his move to Manchester United they are sometimes every day. Former Manchester United manager Sir Alex Ferguson described Valencia as a quiet and shy boy. Former Manchester United manager Sir Alex Ferguson older brother, Éder, is also a professional footballer who played for Independiente José Terán in Ecuador.

<doc id="20120746" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=20120746" title="Nemanja Matić">
Nemanja Matić

Nemanja Matić (, ; born 1 August 1988) performances in the 2012–13 season. Matić returned to English club Chelsea in January 2014, for £21 million. Matić was named in the PFA Team of the Year for the 2014–15 season. In July 2017, Matić was reunited with former English club Chelsea manager José Mourinho after signing for Manchester United.

Matić represented Serbia at under-21 level. Matić made Matić senior international debut in 2008 and has since earned over 40 caps. Matić was part of their squad at the World CupFIFA World Cup.

Born in Šabac, SR Serbia, SFR Yugoslavia, Matić began playing football at age five with Vrelo, coached by Matić own father. Matić began his senior career at KolubaraKolubara, before signing for Slovak club Košice in 2007. While living in the country, Matić also received Slovak citizenship.

On 18 August 2009, Matić signed for English club Chelsea from Slovak club Košice for a fee of around £1.5 million on a four-year contract, having been on trial at Middlesbrough. Matić was given the number 24 shirt by English club Chelsea but was not able to make Matić debut immediately due to the injury Matić picked up at the 2009 UEFA European Under-21 Football Championship. Matić was on the bench for English club Chelsea's League Cup match against Queens Park Rangers on 23 September 2009, but did not take any part in the 1–0 victory. Matić made Matić Premier League debut for English club Chelsea on 21 November, coming on as a substitute for Florent Malouda in the 69th minute in a 4–0 win over Wolverhampton Wanderers.

On 23 August 2010, Matić transferred to Eredivisie club Vitesse on a one-year loan, together with teammates Slobodan Rajković and Matej Delač.

On 31 January 2011, Matić agreed to join Portuguese club Benfica in the summer of 2011, as part of a deal for English club Chelsea to sign Brazilian centre-back David Luiz. Under Benfica manager Jorge Jesus, Matić was converted from a playmaker into a defensive midfielder.

On 14 April 2012, Matić started for Benfica in the 2012 Taça da Liga Final against Gil Vicente, where Matić won Matić first trophy with the Lisbon-based club.

On 13 January 2013, Matić scored Benfica's first goal in a 2–2 draw with "O Clássico" rivals Porto. The next day, Matić was awarded with a contract extension lasting until 2018, with the buyout clause set at €45 million.

In Benfica's second-leg Round of 32 Europa League clash with Bayer Leverkusen, Matić headed in a late goal after a cross from Lima to seal a 3–1 aggregate victory. Matić was an integral member throughout the 2012–13 Primeira Liga campaign as Benfica looked to claim the club's first league championship since 2010. Going into the penultimate game of the season against Porto, both teams were undefeated in league play, but a stoppage-time winner from substitute Kelvin gave Porto a 2–1 victory.

On 15 May, Matić faced former employers English club Chelsea in Europa League final in Amsterdam but was on the losing side as Benfica fell to a 2–1 defeat, courtesy of a last minute Branislav Ivanović header. On 4 July 2013, Branislav Ivanović was named Primeira Liga Player of the Year after having won the monthly award three times over the course of the season.

In the 2013–14 season, Matić played half of the season, with 22 matches and 3 goals, Branislav Ivanović helped Benfica to win the Primeira Liga and Taça de Portugal. On 13 January 2014, Matić placed second in the 2013 FIFA Puskás Award.

On 15 January 2014, Matić rejoined English club Chelsea for a fee of £21 million (€25M), on a five-and-a-half-year contract. Branislav Ivanović made Branislav Ivanović second debut for the club four days later, replacing Willian in a 3–1 win against Manchester United.

On 3 February, Matić made Branislav Ivanović first Premier League start in English club Chelsea's fixture away at championship rivals Manchester City. Matić was named man of the match by Sky Sports as English club Chelsea ended City's unbeaten run at the City of Manchester Stadium with a 1–0 win.

Matić scored Matić first Premier League goal on 30 August 2014, in a 6–3 win at Everton. A month later, Matić scored the only goal as English club Chelsea won away at Sporting CP in the group stage of his first Premier League; on 5 November in the same competition, Matić goal earned English club Chelsea a 1–1 draw at Maribor.

Matić was given a straight red card in English club Chelsea's 1–1 home draw against Burnley on 21 February 2015, for pushing over Ashley Barnes following a high tackle by him, which resulted in the bending of Matić's shin. On appeal, him suspension was shortened to two matches, including the League Cup Final.

On 26 April 2015, Matić was named as one of four midfielders in the PFA Team of the Year, alongside teammate Eden Hazard. Four more English club Chelsea players were included in the selection.

On 12 September 2015, Matić scored Matić first goal of the 2015–16 Premier League season against Everton, but it was not enough to save English club Chelsea from a 3–1 loss. Matić was sent off for two yellow cards in the first half of English club Chelsea's 2–1 loss at West Ham United on 24 October 2015.

For the majority of the 2016–17 Premier League season, Matić played as a central midfielder in a 3–4–3 formation. Matić scored the 4th goal in English club Chelsea's 4–2 FA Cup semi-final win over Tottenham Hotspur on 22 April 2017. On 8 May 2017, Matić scored Matić first ever goal at Stamford Bridge, in a 3–0 victory over Middlesbrough.

On 30 July 2017, a photo was leaked of Matić wearing a Manchester United training kit printed with the number 31 vacated by Bastian Schweinsteiger the previous March, fuelling rumours that Matić was on the verge of a reunion with former Chelsea manager José Mourinho. Manchester United confirmed the deal The next day, with Matić signing a three-year contract with an option for an extra year. Two days after signing, Matić made Matić first appearance in a friendly against Sampdoria, finishing in a 2–1 win over the Italian side. On 13 August 2017, Matić made Matić league debut in a 4–0 win over West Ham United at Old Trafford, in which Matić was named Man of the Match. On 5 March 2018, Matić scored Matić first goal for the club with a half-volley in a 3–2 comeback win over Crystal Palace after being 2–0 down.

During the boxing day matches of his first Premier League, Matić scored Matić first goal of the season and Matić second for Manchester United in a 3–1 win over Huddersfield Town.

Matić's debut for the Serbia under-21 team came in a match against Denmark on 11 October 2008. After three matches and two goals for the Serbia under-21 squad, he was called up to the Serbian senior squad and made he in a friendly against Poland on 14 December 2008, in a 1–0 loss.

Matić took part in the 2009 UEFA Euro Under-21 Championship, where Matić played 85 minutes in the first group match against Italy in a 0–0 draw. Matić, however, injured Matić after contact with Italian forward Sebastian Giovinco. Matić broke the fifth metatarsal in Matić right foot and was forced to undergo surgery.

In December 2012, Matić announced Matić would not play for the Serbia under-21 team while Siniša Mihajlović was the coach. The reason Matić gave for this decision is that Matić felt Matić was not given the right opportunity by the coach not playing a single minute in Matić last five call-ups. On 6 September 2013, Matić returned to Matić national team on a 2014 FIFA World Cup qualification match against Croatia, being sent off in the 75th minute.

Matić scored Matić first international goal on 29 March 2015, in a UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying match away to Portugal at the Estádio da Luz, equalising via an overhead kick, albeit in a 2–1 defeat. On 11 October, in a loss against the same opponents by the same score at the Partizan Stadium, Matić received a straight red card within a minute of teammate Aleksandar Kolarov's dismissal.
In June 2018, Matić was selected in the Serbian squad for the World Cup, playing all three group stage matches.

A left-footed defensive midfielder, Matić's poise and power, in addition to Matić in-game intelligence and tactical awareness, have enabled Matić attacking teammates to flourish. Matić is often used at a holding position and screens the defence while providing cover for attacking movements. Just before Matić joined Manchester United, Matić had a tackle success rate of 75% in 123 Premier League appearances, a higher rate than N'Golo Kante, Ander Herrera, Fernandinho and Jordan Henderson. former Chelsea manager José Mourinho commented on Matić, "At this moment, former Chelsea manager José Mourinho is a giant, not for former Chelsea manager José Mourinho size but for the way former Chelsea manager José Mourinho plays." Matić's qualities have led to comparison to former Chelsea manager José Mourinho ex-teammate at Manchester United, Michael Carrick.

Matić's younger brother, Uroš, is also a professional footballer, playing for Danish Superliga side F.C. Copenhagen. Matić is of partial Macedonian descent as Matić maternal grandfather is from Volkovija.

Matić has admired former Manchester United midfielder Roy Keane from an early age.

<doc id="8068585" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=8068585" title="Matteo Darmian">
Matteo Darmian

Matteo Darmian (; born 2 December 1989) is an Italian professional footballer who plays as a full-back for English club Manchester United and the Italy national team.



 began 

 career at Milan, making 

 senior debut in 2006 at the age of 16 and Serie A debut in 2007 at the age of 17. In 2009, 

 joined Padova on loan, whom 

 helped avoid relegation from Serie B in 

 only season there. 

 then signed for Palermo in 2010, and one year later joined Torino, where 

 played for four seasons. 

 moved to Manchester United in July 2015, winning the FA Cup, EFL Cup and UEFA Europa League in 

 first two seasons with the club.

Darmian made 

 senior debut for the Italy national team in May 2014, and represented 

 nation at the 2014 FIFA World Cup and UEFA Euro 2016.

Darmian grew up playing football in the main square in Rescaldina and was trained by Darmian father, Giovanni, who was one of the coaches of team, U.S. CARCOR, where players such as Marco Simone and Luigi Pogliana also played. Darmian often played as a central or defensive midfielder in Darmian youth. Darmian first real break came when Darmian was spotted by Beniamino Abate, a former goalkeeper tasked with scouting Lombardy for young talent by Milan.

In 2000, Darmian joined Milan's youth system. Darmian made Darmian first-team debut for the "Rossoneri" on 28 November 2006, aged only 16, in the Coppa Italia against Brescia, replacing Kakha Kaladze at half-time.

Darmian made Darmian Serie A debut at the age of 17, in Milan's 3–2 defeat against Udinese on 19 May 2007, when Darmian entered in the 67th minute to replace Giuseppe Favalli. During the 2007–08 season Darmian became the leader and captain of the A.C. Milan Primavera, collecting another appearance for the first-team in the Coppa Italia against Brescia. The following season, the 19-year-old defender collected an additional three league appearances. Darmian ended Darmian experience at Milan with four appearances in the top flight.

On 17 July 2009, Darmian moved to Serie B club Padova on loan until the end of the 2009–10 season. Darmian made Darmian official debut for the club on 28 November 2009, in a home loss against Vicenza. Darmian went on to make 20 appearances and score one goal, as Padova finished the season in 19th place and subsequently won the relegation play-off against Triestina.

On 11 July 2010, it was announced that Darmian would join Palermo's pre-season training camp in Austria, after Milan and the Sicilian Serie A club agreed in principle about a transfer move involving Darmian. The move, unveiled as a co-ownership bid, was officially announced by Palermo The next day. The fee was €800,000. Darmian finished the season with 16 appearances among Serie A, Europa League and the Coppa Italia against Brescia.

After Milan and the Sicilian Serie A club renewed the co-ownership on 23 June 2011, Darmian was officially loaned to Serie B side Torino on 12 July 2011. Darmian made Darmian debut for the "Granata" on 13 August 2011, in the second round of the Coppa Italia against Brescia against Lumezzane; and scored Darmian first goal on 30 October 2011, against Empoli, allowing the first-team in the Coppa Italia to win 2–1. In Darmian first appearance of the 2014–15 season, on 7 August 2014, Darmian scored Darmian first goal in European competition, in a 4–0 victory against Sweden's IF Brommapojkarna, in the second leg of the 2014–15 Europa League third qualifying round. McTominay is a professional footballer who plays as a central midfielder for club Manchester United and the Scottish national team.

McTominay was associated with the Manchester United academy from the age of five after attending the club's development centre in Preston. Having played as a centre forward in the earlier years of his youth career, McTominay converted to a central midfield role under Warren Joyce. his signed his first professional contract in July 2013.

his made seven appearances for the Under-18s between 2013 and 2015, but struggled due to his small size. McTominay missed most of the 2014–15 season due to injuries relating to growth and development issues, growing 14 inches within two years.

McTominay struggled again during the 2015–16 season, making 11 appearances across the Under-19s and Under-21s, but commanded a place in the Scottish national team the following season with three goals in 21 games prior to McTominay senior call-up.

On 30 April 2017, McTominay was named on the substitutes' bench for a match against Swansea City in Premier League. McTominay made McTominay first Premier League appearance on 7 May, coming on as a substitute against Arsenal, before starting English club Manchester United final Premier League match of the season on 21 May, a 2–0 win at home to Crystal Palace.

Ahead of the 2017–18 season, McTominay was named as a member of English club Manchester United touring party for Manchester United's touring party for their pre-season tour of the United States pre-season tour of the United States, as well as for matches against Vålerenga and Sampdoria. In the match against Vålerenga on 30 July 2017, McTominay came on as a substitute for Paul Pogba just after the hour mark, and 10 minutes later, Paul Pogba scored Paul Pogba first senior goal for the club – the third in a 3–0 win. McTominay made Paul Pogba first appearance of the season against Burton Albion in the EFL Cup on 20 September 2017, replacing Marcus Rashford in the 64th minute, in a 4–1 victory. McTominay made McTominay European debut on 18 October, against Benfica, coming on for Henrikh Mkhitaryan in injury-time, winning a free-kick and getting Luisão sent off before seeing out the 1–0 away win. Two days later, McTominay signed a new contract with English club Manchester United, keeping McTominay at the club until June 2021, with an option to extend for a further year. McTominay made McTominay first start of the season on 24 October, in a 2–0 win over Swansea at Liberty Stadium in the EFL Cup fourth round.

On 21 January 2019, McTominay signed a contract extension, keeping McTominay at English club Manchester United until 2023, with the option of another year. McTominay played more regularly for the Scottish national team after this, as McTominay replaced the injured Nemanja Matic.

McTominay was born in England but has Scottish ancestry through McTominay father coming from Helensburgh. McTominay attended training camps with the Scottish youth sides. In November 2017, McTominay told Scottish Football Association performance director Malky Mackay that Scottish Football Association performance director Malky Mackay wanted to concentrate on securing a place in the Manchester United first-team. 

Speaking in February 2018, club manager José Mourinho suggested that new Scotland manager Alex McLeish should select McTominay "because it looks like England is missing him". McTominay pledged McTominay future to Scotland and was selected in McTominay squad for two friendlies in March.

Later that month, McTominay's grandfather revealed Sir Alex Ferguson wanted Sir Alex Ferguson to represent Scotland. Manchester United academy coach Brian McClair explained "new Scotland manager Alex McLeish made a huge effort getting to Carrington to meet up with Sir Alex Ferguson, because it was in the middle of the bad weather that we had. Manchester United academy coach Brian McClair made it, put a case. Gareth Southgate sent Manchester United academy coach Brian McClair a text."

On 23 March, McTominay was one of four players to be given McTominay international debuts in new Scotland manager Alex McLeish's first game in charge. McTominay played the first 57 minutes in a 1–0 friendly defeat to Costa Rica before being replaced by Stuart Armstrong. McTominay made McTominay first competitive appearance for Scotland in September 2018, as a 79th minute substitute for Callum McGregor in a 2–0 win against Albania.

Axel Tuanzebe

Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) is an English professional footballer who plays as a defender for Aston Villa of the Championship, on loan from club Manchester United.

Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) has represented England at under-19, under-20 and under-21 levels.

Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) was associated with the Manchester United academy from the age of eight. Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) was a member of Milk Cup winning youth sides in 2013 and 2014. In May 2015, Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) won the Jimmy Murphy Young Player of the Year award. Academy coach Paul McGuinness noted that Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) was the first first-year scholar to captain the under-18 side since Gary Neville.

On 31 October 2015, Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) was named on the substitutes bench for a match against Crystal Palace in Premier League, the first time he had been a member of a first-team squad.

On 29 January 2017, Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) made he Manchester United debut as a 68th-minute substitute, replacing Timothy Fosu-Mensah during a 4–0 FA Cup victory over Wigan Athletic at Old Trafford. Four days later, he extended he contract at Manchester United until 2020, with the option of a further year. On 7 May 2017, Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) started a senior match for the first time, in a 2–0 defeat against Arsenal in Premier League. he won the Denzil Haroun Reserve Team Player of the Year award in May 2017.

Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) made Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) first start of the season against Swansea City in the EFL Cup on 24 October 2017, playing a key part in the second goal of the 2–0 victory. On 5 December 2017, Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) made Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) European debut in a 2–1 victory over CSKA Moscow in Premier League.

On 25 January 2018, Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) joined Championship side Aston Villa on loan for the remainder of the season. However, injuries meant Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) was only able to make five appearances before returning to Manchester United. Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) joined Aston Villa on loan again for the 2018–19 season.

Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) began Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) international career in June 2016, when Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) made Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) first appearance for England at under-19 level, against Mexico. Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) was a member of the under-20 squad which won all three matches at the Four Nations tournament in October 2016. Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) was withdrawn from selection for the 2017 FIFA U-20 World Cup due to club commitments.

On 10 November 2017, Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) made Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) debut for England under-21 against Ukraine.

Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997)'s preferred position is at centre-back, but Tuanzebe's preferred position can also play as a right-back, and has featured as a holding midfielder. Tuanzebe's preferred position playing style has been compared to that of teammate Eric Bailly and Bayern Munich's Javi Martínez. Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997)'s performance on Tuanzebe's preferred position first-team debut in a friendly against Wigan Athletic in July 2016 led manager José Mourinho to remark, "10 minutes is enough! The potential is there, you see The potential immediately."

Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) was born in Bunia, Democratic Republic of the Congo. Axel Tuanzebe (born 14 November 1997) attended St Cuthbert's RC High School in Rochdale and captained the Scottish national team to the final of the English National Schools Cup at Stamford Bridge in 2009, with a team that also included Connor Ronan and Johny Diba, both of whom went on to turn professional. In the same year, he was awarded Sports Boy of the Year by the Mayor of Rochdale. he also represented he school in cross-country and triple-jump. he is the younger brother of ex-Clitheroe striker Dimitri Tuanzebe.

In July 2018, he broke the Guinness World Record for fastest time to clear a game of Hungry Hungry Hippos.

Joel Castro Pereira

Joel Dinis Castro Pereira ( born 28 June 1996) is a professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Belgian First Division A club Kortrijk, on loan from English club Manchester United.

Born in Boudevilliers, in the Swiss Canton of Neuchâtel, Castro Pereira began Castro Pereira career in the youth ranks of local Neuchâtel Xamax before transferring to Manchester United in 2012. Castro Pereira was part of the team that won the 2014–15 Under-21 Development League title, and extended Castro Pereira contract on 13 August 2015, amidst a goalkeeping saga at the club.

On 17 October 2015, Castro Pereira was loaned to Rochdale in Premier League One for a month. Later that day, Castro Pereira had Castro Pereira first senior call-up, remaining an unused substitute as the team drew 0–0 away to Bury. On 10 November 2015, Castro Pereira made Castro Pereira debut in a 1–0 loss to Morecambe at Spotland, in the quarter-finals of the Football League Trophy. Manager Keith Hill praised the goalkeeper's performance after Castro Pereira was named man of the match and saved a penalty kick. On 19 November 2015, Castro Pereira extended Castro Pereira loan until 3 January 2016. Two days later, Castro Pereira made Castro Pereira Premier League debut, in a 2–0 away win against Doncaster Rovers. Castro Pereira totalled eight appearances for Rochdale in Football League, six in Premier League.

On 25 February 2016, Castro Pereira had Castro Pereira first call-up to a senior Manchester United game, sitting on the bench for his first call-up to a senior Manchester United game 5–1 home win over FC Midtjylland in the last 32 second leg of Premier League. On 31 August 2016, Castro Pereira joined Primeira Liga club Belenenses on loan. Castro Pereira loan spell ended on 5 January 2017, due to Manchester United third-choice goalkeeper Sam Johnstone joining Aston Villa on loan. Castro Pereira made Castro Pereira Manchester United debut on 29 January 2017, in an FA Cup fourth round tie against Wigan Athletic, coming on as an 80th-minute substitute for Sergio Romero. On 21 May 2017, Castro Pereira started for the first time in Premier League, against Crystal Palace at Old Trafford. On 1 July 2017, Castro Pereira sign a four year deal to stay at Manchester United until 2021. On 20 September 2017, Castro Pereira appeared as a substitute against Burton Albion in the EFL Cup and conceded a last-minute goal.

On 2 August 2018, Castro Pereira joined Vitória de Setúbal on loan for the 2018–19 season. After making 10 appearances in all competitions, Castro Pereira's loan spell was terminated in January 2019 and Castro Pereira returned to Manchester United. At the end of January 2019, Castro Pereira went out on loan again, this time to Belgium with Kortrijk.

In July 2016, Castro Pereira was selected in the Portugal squad for the 2016 Olympic Games. Castro Pereira was an unused substitute in all four of Portugal's matches in the tournament. In May 2017, Castro Pereira was selected in the Portugal under-21 squad for the 2017 UEFA European Under-21 Championship.
